GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 37.01 TELEPHONE AND BROADBAND INTERNET EXCHANGE INSPECTION FEE AND CHARGE.
   There is hereby levied an annual inspection fee and service charge upon each
and every person, firm and corporation operating a telephone and broadband
internet exchange in the city in an amount equal to 2% of the gross revenues
for each current year for exchange telephone and broadband internet
transmission service rendered wholly within the limits of the city to
compensate the city for the expense incurred and services rendered incident to
the exercise of its police power, supervision, police regulation and police
control of the construction of lines and equipment of the telephone company in
the city.
(1999 Code, § 37.01) (Ord. passed 4-4-2019)
§ 37.02 UTILITY TAX.
   (A)   Utility tax levied. There is hereby levied and assessed an annual tax
of 2% upon gross receipts from residential and commercial sales of gas,
electricity and cable services within the city, which tax shall be in lieu of
any other franchise, license, occupation or excise tax levied by the city, in
accordance with the provisions of 68 O.S. §§ 2601 through 2605, as amended and
supplemented, and other applicable provisions of state law.
   (B)   Not to apply to franchise. The tax levied under this section shall,
when levied, apply to all persons, firms, associations or corporations engaged
in the business of furnishing gas, electricity or cable services within the
city limits, except it shall not apply to any person, firm, association or
corporation operating under a valid franchise from the city granted pursuant to
Article 18, § 5(a) of the Oklahoma Constitution, nor shall it apply to those
entities exempt from taxation under applicable provisions of state law.
   (C)   Payment of tax. The tax levied under this section shall be levied for
a term of not less than one year and shall be payable quarterly, on or prior to
the tenth day of the months of January, April, July and October of each year,
as applicable, and the proceeds thereof shall be placed in the General Revenue
Fund of the city.
   (D)   Failure to pay tax. Any person, firm, association or corporation
failing or refusing to pay such tax when levied shall be regarded as a
trespasser and may be ousted from the city, and in addition thereto, an action
may be maintained against such person, firm, association or corporation for the
amount of the tax, and all expenses of collecting same, including reasonable
attorney fees.
   (E)   Tax constitutes lien. The tax so imposed shall constitute a first and
prior lien on all assets located within the city of any person, firm,
association or corporation engaged in the business of selling utility services
within the municipal limits of the city.
   (F)   Record of sales.
      (1)   It shall be the duty of any person, firm, association or
corporation subject to the tax levied hereunder to keep and maintain records as
to the amount of gross receipts of sales of gas, electricity and cable services
to the city, and such records shall be subject to review and audit by the city
upon reasonable request.
      (2)   In addition, a summary of such sales for the preceding calendar
quarter, including the number of customers served, the number of customers
exempt from taxation under applicable state sales tax laws, the number of units
of gas and electricity and cable services (cubic feet or kilowatt hours,
respectively) sold to exempt and non-exempt customers, the gross receipts from
sales tax charged and collected with respect to such sales, shall be provided
to the city at the time of payment of the tax pursuant to division (C) above.
(1999 Code, § 37.02) (Ord. 111, passed 11-4-1996)
SALES TAX
§ 37.15 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known and may be cited as the “City of Hooker Sales
Tax Ordinance Number Two” and is hereinafter referred to as “subchapter”.
(1999 Code, § 37.15) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.16 PURPOSE.
   It is hereby declared to be the purpose of this subchapter to provide
revenues for support of general municipal functions.
(1999 Code, § 37.16) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.17 EFFECTIVE DATE; DURATION OF TAX.
   This subchapter shall become and be effective on and after October 1, 1977,
subject to approval of a majority of the registered voters of the city voting
on same in the manner prescribed state law. This subchapter shall continue in
full force and effect until repealed.
(1999 Code, § 37.17) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.18 EFFECT ON OTHER TAXES.
   The provisions hereof shall be cumulative and in addition to any and all
other taxing provisions of city ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 37.18) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.19 EFFECT ON EXISTING STATE PERMITS.
   All valid and subsisting permits to do business issued by the State Tax
Commission pursuant to the State Sales Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq.
are, for the purposes of this subchapter, hereby ratified, confirmed and
adopted in lieu of any requirement for an additional city permit for the same
purpose.
(1999 Code, § 37.19) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.20 AMENDMENTS.
   The people of the city, by their approval of this subchapter at the election
provided in §
37.17, hereby authorize the City Council by ordinances duly enacted to make
such administrative and technical changes or additions in the method and manner
of administering and enforcing this subchapter as may be necessary or proper
for efficiency and fairness, except that the rate of the tax herein provided
shall not be changed without approval of the qualified electors of the city as
provided by law.
(1999 Code, § 37.20) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.21 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   The definitions of words, terms and phrases contained in the State
Sales Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq., are hereby adopted by reference
and made a part of this subchapter.
   (B)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      TAX COLLECTOR. The department of the city government or the official
agency of the state duly designated, according to law or contract authorized by
law, to administer the collection of the tax herein levied.
(1999 Code, § 37.21) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.22 TAX RATE; TAXABLE SALES.
   (A)   Tax rate; sales subject to tax. There is hereby levied an excise tax
of 4% upon the gross proceeds or gross receipts derived from all sales taxable
under the sales tax law of the state, including but not exclusive of the
following:
      (1)   Tangible personal property;
      (2)   Natural or artificial gas, electricity, ice, steam or any other
utility or public service, except water;
      (3)   Transportation for hire or persons by common carriers, including
railroads, both steam and electric, motor transportation companies, taxicab
companies, Pullman car companies, airlines and all other means of
transportation for hire;
      (4)   Service by telephone and internet companies to subscribers or
users, including transmission of messages, whether local or long distance. This
shall include all services and rental charges having any connection with
transmission of any message;
      (5)   Printing or printed matter of all types, kinds and characters and
the service of printing or overprinting;
      (6)   Service of furnishing rooms by hotels, apartment hotels, public
rooming houses and public lodging houses and tourist camps;
      (7)   Service of furnishing storage or parking privileges by auto hotels
and parking lots;
      (8)   Carrier sales of newspapers and periodicals made directly to
consumers. Other sales of newspapers and periodicals where any individual
transaction does not exceed $1. A CARRIER is a person who regularly delivers
newspapers or periodicals to subscribers on an assigned route;
      (9)   Advertising of all kinds, types and character, including any and
all devices used for advertising purposes and the servicing of any advertising
devices, except as provided in §
37.23(A)(14);
      (10)   Dues or fees to clubs, and the sale of tickets or admission to
places of amusement or athletic, entertainment or recreational events, or dues
or fees for the privilege of having access to or the use of amusement,
entertainment, athletic or recreational facilities, including free or
complimentary passes. Tickets, dues or fees are hereby declared to have a value
equivalent to the sale price of tickets, passes, admissions, fees or dues of
like kind or character; and
      (11)   (a)   The sale, preparation or service of ice or nonalcoholic
beverages that are sold, prepared or served for the purpose of being mixed with
alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises where such sale,
preparation or service occurs.
         (b)   The total retail sale price received for the sale, preparation
or service of ice or nonalcoholic beverages to be mixed with alcoholic
beverages for consumption on the premises where such sale, preparation and
service occurs shall constitute the gross receipts from such transaction.
   (B)   Deemed sales to consumers or users.
      (1)   For the purpose of this subchapter, sales of service and tangible
personal property made for the purpose of developing real estate, even though
such real estate is intended for resale as real property, are hereby declared
to be sales to consumers or users.
      (2)   Sales of service and tangible personal property, including
materials, supplies and equipment made to contractors who use same in the
performance of any contract, are hereby declared to be sales to consumers or
users and not sales for resale.
      (3)   Sales of tangible personal property to persons who are primarily
engaged in selling their services shall be deemed sales to consumers or users
and, therefore, taxable.
      (4)   Sales of tangible personal property to peddlers, solicitors and
other salespersons who do not have established places of business shall be
deemed to be sales to consumers or users and, therefore, taxable.
   (C)   Additional tax.
      (1)   Citations and codification. This division (C) shall be known and
may be cited as the “City of Hooker Sales Tax Ordinance of 2008”, and the same
shall be codified and incorporated into the code of ordinances of the city.
      (2)   Tax imposed. There is hereby imposed an excise tax of 1% (in
addition to any and all other excise taxes now in force) to be levied upon the
gross proceeds or gross receipts derived from all sales taxable under the State
Sales Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq.
      (3)   Purpose of revenues. It is hereby declared to be the purpose of
this division (C) to provide revenues of 0.5% to be used for the City Fire
Department and Ambulance Service and for the City Treasurer to set up a new
cash account to be used from date of approval forward entitled “Emergency
Services” for the funds to be placed in for the Fire Department and EMS; 0.25%
to be divided equally for the benefit of the city municipal pool, city parks,
city library and cemetery; and 0.25% for the General Fund of the city, and any
public trust having the city as beneficiary thereof and/or for the payment of
debt service in connection with obligations issued to finance said capital
expenditures.
      (4)   Effective date. The provisions of this division (C) and the
collection of the excise tax referenced herein shall become effective on and
after January 1, 2009, subject to approval by a majority of the qualified
electors of the city voting on the same in the manner prescribed by law.
      (5)   No repeal of tax. This division (C) and the excise tax levied
pursuant hereto shall not be repealed by the City Council or by referendum of
the registered qualified voters of the city in the event the proceeds of the
referenced excise tax are being used or have been pledged by the city of any
public trust having the city as beneficiary for the purpose of paying debt
service on obligations issued by the city or any public trust having the city
as beneficiary.
      (6)   Subsisting state permits. All valid and subsisting permits to do
business issued by the State Tax Commission pursuant to the State Sales Tax
Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq. are, for the purposes of this division (C),
hereby ratified, confirmed and adopted in lieu of any requirement for an
additional city permit for the same purpose.
      (7)   Payment of tax. The tax herein levied shall be paid to the Tax
Collector at the time and in the manner and form prescribed for payment of the
state sales tax under the state tax law.
      (8)   This tax in addition to taxes currently levied; administrative
procedures. The tax levied hereby is in addition to any and all other excise
taxes levied or assessed by the city including those levied and assessed by
Ord. 11 and Ord. 32; provided, however, that those provisions of said
ordinances relating to definitions; Tax Collector defined; classification of
taxpayers; subsisting state permits; the portion of tax rate—sales subject to
tax, pertaining to sales subject to tax; the provisions of said ordinances
regarding exemptions and other exempt transfers; the provisions of said
ordinances regarding tax due when— returns—records; the portion of said
ordinances regarding tax constituting debt; vendor’s duty to collect tax;
returns and remittances; interest and penalties—delinquency; waiver of interest
and penalties; erroneous payments—claim for refund; fraudulent returns; and
records confidential shall apply to the excise tax levied and assessed by this
subchapter. For purposes of this division (C), references in Ord. 11 and Ord.
32, to specific provisions of the Oklahoma Statutes shall be deemed to be
references to said statutory provisions, as amended.
      (9)   Amendments. The people of the city, by their approval of this
division (C) at an election hereby authorize the city by ordinance duly enacted
to make such administrative and technical changes or additions in the method
and manner of administration and enforcing this division (C) as may be
necessary or proper for efficiency and fairness or in order to make the same
consistent with the State Sales Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq., as
amended, except that the rate of the tax herein provided for shall not be
changed without approval of the qualified electors of the city as provided by
law.
      (10)   Provisions cumulative. The provisions hereof shall be cumulative
and in addition to any and all other taxing provisions of city ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 37.22) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
71, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 73, passed 1-6-1986; Ord. 120, passed 10-5-1998; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. 2008-3, passed 8-14-2008; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.23 EXEMPT SALES.
   (A)   Generally. There are hereby specifically exempted from the tax levied
by this subchapter the gross receipts of gross proceeds exempted from the sales
tax law of the state, inclusive but not exclusive of, and derived from, the
following:
      (1)   Sale of nonintoxicating beverages taxed as provided by state law;
      (2)   Sale of cigarettes and such tobacco products as are taxed by state
law;
      (3)   Sale of raw products from the farm, orchard or garden, where such
sale is made by the producer of such raw products directly to the consumer or
user; gross receipts or gross proceeds derived from the sale of livestock,
poultry, poultry products and dairy products by the producers; exemptions
granted by this division (A)(3) shall not apply when such articles are sold,
even though by the producer thereof, at or from an “established business place”
not on a farm; neither shall this exemption apply unless said articles are
produced or grown with this state. The provisions of this division (A)(3) are
intended to exempt the sale by livestock producers of livestock sold at special
livestock sales. The provisions of this division (A)(3) are intended to exempt
the sale of dairy products when sold by a dairyperson or farmer who owns all of
the cows from which the dairy products he or she sells are produced. The
provisions of this division (A)(3) shall not be construed to exempt sales of
dairy products by any other business. The provisions of this division (A)(3)
shall not be construed to exempt sales by florists, nurserypersons and chicken
hatcheries;
      (4)   Dues paid to fraternal, religious, civic, charitable or educational
societies or organizations by regular members thereof, provided that such
societies or organizations operate under what is commonly termed the lodge plan
or system and provided that such societies or organizations do not operate for
a profit which inures to the benefit of any individual member or members
thereof to the exclusion of other members;
      (5)   Sale of tangible personal property or services to or by churches,
except where such organization may be engaged in business for profit or
savings, competing with other persons engaged in the same or similar business;
      (6)   (a)   Gross receipts and gross proceeds deriving from the
transportation of school children to and from schools and high schools in motor
and other vehicles; and
         (b)   Transportation of persons where the fare of each person does not
exceed $0.15 or local transportation of persons within the corporate limits of
cities and towns except by taxicabs.
      (7)   Sale of food in public, common, high school or college cafeterias
and lunch rooms operated primarily for teachers and pupils, not operated
primarily for the public and not operated for profit;
      (8)   Carrier sales made directly to consumers or users of newspapers or
any other periodicals where any individual transaction does not exceed $1.50;
      (9)   Sales to the United States government, the state or any of its
political subdivisions;
      (10)   Sale of gasoline or motor fuel on which the motor fuel tax,
gasoline excise tax or special fuels tax has been paid to the state;
      (11)   Sale of crude petroleum or natural or casinghead gas and other
products subject to gross production tax under the provisions of the laws of
this state. This exemption shall not apply when such products are sold to a
consumer or user for consumption or use, except when used for injection into
the earth for the purpose of promoting or facilitating the production of oil or
gas;
      (12)   Sales of motor vehicles, attached optional equipment and
accessories, on which sale the state motor vehicle excise tax has been paid;
      (13)   Sales by county, district and state fairs;
      (14)   Sale of advertising space in newspapers and periodicals and
billboard advertising service, and sales of time for radio and television
broadcasts of advertising;
      (15)   (a)   Sales for resale to persons regularly engaged in the
business of reselling the articles purchased, whether within or without the
state, provided that such sales to residents of this state are made to persons
to whom sales tax permits have been issued by the State Tax Commission as
provided by law. This exemption shall not apply to the sales of articles made
to persons holding permits when such persons purchase items for their use and
which they are not regularly engaged in the business of reselling; neither
shall this exemption apply to sales of tangible personal property to peddlers,
solicitors and other salespersons who do not have sales tax permits or
established places of business; and
         (b)   Goods, wares, merchandise and property sold for use in
manufacturing, compounding, processing, assembling or preparing for sale shall
be classified as having been sold for the purpose of resale or the subject
matter of resale only in the event:
            1.   Such goods, wares, merchandise or property is purchased for
the purpose of being manufactured into a finished article and if it becomes a
recognizable, integral part of the manufactured, compounded, processed,
assembled or prepared products; or
            2.   If it is consumed in the process of manufacturing,
compounding, processing, assembling or preparing products for resale.
      (16)   Sale of machinery and equipment purchased and used by persons
establishing new manufacturing or processing plants in this state, and
machinery and equipment purchased and used by persons in the operation of
manufacturing plants already established in this state, provided that this
exemption shall not apply unless such machinery and equipment is incorporated
into, and is directly used in, the process of manufacturing property subject to
taxation hereunder. The term MANUFACTURING PLANTS shall mean those
establishments primarily engaged in manufacturing or processing operations, and
generally recognized as such;
      (17)   Sale of tangible personal property manufactured in this state when
sold by the manufacturer to a person who transports it to another state for
immediate and exclusive use in some other state;
      (18)   Sale of an interest in tangible personal property to a partner or
other person who after such sale owns a joint interest in such tangible
personal property where the state sales or use tax has previously been paid on
such tangible personal property;
      (19)   Sales of containers shall be exempt when sold to a person
regularly engaged in the business of reselling empty or filled containers, or
when the person purchases such containers for the purpose of packaging raw
products of farm, garden or orchard for resale to the consumer or processor,
provided that this exemption shall not apply to the sale of containers used
more than once and which are ordinarily known as returnable containers unless a
tax under this title is collected and paid to the Tax Collector with respect to
each and every transfer by such person of title or possession of such
returnable container if made to any consumer or user within this state; nor
shall it apply to the sale of labels or other materials delivered along with
items sold but which are not necessary or absolutely essential to the sale of
the sold merchandise;
      (20)   Exemptions of poultry and livestock feed, farm machinery and baby
chicks, turkeys, poults and starter pullets, as prescribed by the State Sales
Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq., shall be equally applicable as
exemptions from the tax herein levied. See divisions (B)(2) and (B)(3) below;
      (21)   Sales to council organizations or similar state supervisory
organizations of the Boy Scouts of America, the Girl Scouts of U.S.A. and the
Campfire Girls shall be exempt from sales tax; and
      (22)   The proceeds from any amount separately stated on the ticket of
admission for the repayment of money borrowed by an accredited state-supported
college or university for the purpose of constructing or enlarging any
entertainment facility as prescribed by the State Sales Tax Code, being 68 O.S.
§§ 1351 et seq. shall also be exempt from the tax herein levied.
   (B)   Agricultural supplies and equipment.
      (1)   Exemption of fertilizer. In addition to all other exemptions
allowed by this subchapter, the sales of agricultural fertilizer to persons
regularly engaged for profit in the business of farming and/or ranching which
are exempt from state sales taxes under provisions of 68 O.S. § 1358 shall
likewise be exempt from the city sales tax herein levied.
      (2)   Exemption of farm machinery. In addition to other exemptions
allowed by this subchapter, the sales of farm machinery to be used directly on
a farm or ranch in the production, cultivation, planting, sowing, harvesting,
processing, spraying, preservation or irrigation of any livestock, poultry,
agricultural or dairy products produced from such lands which are exempt from
state sales tax under provision of 68 O.S. § 1358 shall be likewise exempt from
the city sales tax herein levied. Each purchaser of farm machinery must
certify, in writing, on the copy of the invoice or sales ticket to be retained
by the seller that he or she is engaged in farming or ranching and that the
farm machinery will be used in farming or ranching.
      (3)   Exemption of gross proceeds from sale and purchase of feed. In
addition to the other exemptions allowed by this subchapter, the sales and
purchases within the state of feed shall, subject to the conditions and
limitations set forth in 68 O.S. § 1358, also be exempt from the sales tax.
(1999 Code, § 37.23) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.24 EXEMPT TRANSFERS OF PERSONAL PROPERTY.
   Additionally, there is hereby specifically exempted from the tax herein
levied the transfer of tangible personal property exempted from the sales tax
law of the state, inclusive but not exclusive of the following:
   (A)   From one corporation to another corporation pursuant to a
reorganization. As used in this section, the term REORGANIZATION means:
      (1)   A statutory merger or consolidation; and
      (2)   The acquisition by a corporation of substantially all of the
properties of another corporation when the consideration is solely all or a
part of the voting stock of the acquiring corporation, or of its parent or
subsidiary corporation.
   (B)   In connection with the winding up, dissolution or liquidation of a
corporation only when there is distribution in kind to the shareholders of the
property of such corporation;
   (C)   To a corporation for the purpose of organization of such corporation
where the former owners of the property transferred are immediately after the
transfer in control of the corporation, and the stock or securities received by
each is substantially in proportion to this interest in the property prior to
the transfer;
   (D)   To a partnership in the organization of such partnership if the former
owners of the property transferred are immediately after the transfer members
of such partnerships and the interest in the partnership received by each is
substantially in proportion to this interest in the property prior to the
transfer; and
   (E)   From a partnership to the members thereof when made in kind in the
dissolution of such partnership.
(1999 Code, § 37.24) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.25 PAYMENT OF TAX.
   (A)   Tax due when; returns; records. The tax levied hereunder shall be due
and payable at the time and in the form and manner provided for payment of the
state sales tax under the sales tax law of this state.
   (B)   Payment of tax. The tax herein levied shall be paid to the Tax
Collector at the time and in the form and manner provided for payment of state
sales tax under the sales tax law of the state.
(1999 Code, § 37.25) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.26 TAX AS DEBT; TAX PRIORITY.
   Such taxes, penalty and interest due hereunder shall at all times constitute
a prior, superior and paramount claim as against the claims of unsecured
creditors, and may be collected by suit as any other debt.
(1999 Code, § 37.26) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.27 CLASSIFICATION OF TAXPAYERS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the classification of taxpayers
hereunder shall be as prescribed by state law for purposes of the State Sales
Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq.
(1999 Code, § 37.27) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.28 COLLECTION OF TAX BY VENDOR; ADVERTISING.
   (A)   The tax levied hereunder shall be paid by the consumer or user to the
vendor, and it shall be the duty of each and every vendor in this city to
collect from the consumer or user the full amount of the tax levied by this
subchapter, or an amount equal as nearly as possible or practicable to the
average equivalent thereof.
   (B)   Vendors shall add the tax imposed hereunder, or the average equivalent
thereof, to the sales price or charge, and when added such tax shall constitute
a part of such price or charge, shall be a debt from the consumer or user to
the vendor until paid, and shall be recoverable at law in the same manner as
other debts.
   (C)   A vendor, as defined herein, who willfully or intentionally fails,
neglects or refuses to collect the full amount of the tax levied hereof, or
willfully or intentionally fails, neglects or refuses to comply with the
provisions or remits or rebates to a consumer or user, either directly or
indirectly, and by whatsoever means, all or any part of the tax herein levied,
or makes in any form of advertising, verbally or otherwise, any statement which
infers that he or she is absorbing the tax or paying the tax for the consumer
or user by an adjustment of prices or at a price including the tax or in any
manner whatsoever shall be deemed guilty of an offense, and upon conviction
thereof shall be penalized as provided in §
10.99.
(1999 Code, § 37.28) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 37.29 RETURNS AND REMITTANCES; DISCOUNT.
   Returns and remittances of the tax herein levied and collected shall be made
to the Tax Collector at the time, and in the manner, form and amount as
prescribed for returns and remittances required by the State Sales Tax Code,
being 68 O.S. §§ 1351 et seq., and remittances of the tax collected hereunder
shall be subject to the same discount as may be allowed by said code for
collection of state sales taxes.
(1999 Code, § 37.29) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.30 INTEREST AND PENALTIES.
   (A)   Interest and penalties; delinquency. 68 O.S. § 217 is hereby adopted
and made a part of this subchapter, and interest and penalties at the rates and
in amounts as therein specified are hereby levied and shall be applicable in
cases of delinquency in reporting and paying the tax levied by this subchapter,
provided that the failure or refusal of any taxpayer to make and transmit the
reports and remittances of tax in the time and manner required by this
subchapter shall cause such tax to be delinquent. In addition, if such
delinquency continues for a period of five days, the taxpayer shall forfeit his
or her claim to any discount allowed under this subchapter.
   (B)   Waiver of interest and penalties. The interest or penalty or any
portion thereof accruing by reason of a taxpayer’s failure to pay the tax
herein levied may be waived or remitted in the same manner as provided for said
waiver or remittance as applied in administration of the state sales tax
provided in 68 O.S. § 220, and to accomplish the purposes of this section the
applicable provisions of said § 220 are hereby adopted by reference and made a
part of this subchapter.
(1999 Code, § 37.30) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.31 ERRONEOUS PAYMENTS; CLAIM FOR REFUND.
   Refund of erroneous payment of the city sales tax herein levied may be made
to any taxpayer making such erroneous payment in the same manner and procedures
and under the same limitations of time as provided for administration of the
state sales tax as set forth in 68 O.S. § 227, and to accomplish the purposes
of this section the applicable provisions of said § 227 are hereby adopted by
reference and made a part of this subchapter.
(1999 Code, § 37.31) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
§ 37.32 FALSE RETURNS.
   In addition to all civil penalties provided by this subchapter, the willful
failure or refusal of any taxpayer to make reports and remittances therein
required, or the making of any false and fraudulent report for the purpose of
avoiding or escaping payment of any tax or portion thereof rightfully due under
this subchapter shall be an offense, and upon conviction thereof the offending
taxpayer shall be penalized as provided in §
10.99.
(1999 Code, § 37.32) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 37.33 RECORD CONFIDENTIALITY.
   The confidential and privileged nature of the records and files concerning
the administration of the city sales tax is legislatively recognized and
declared, and to protect the same the provisions of 68 O.S. § 205 of the State
Sales Tax Code and each subsection thereof are hereby adopted by reference and
made fully effective and applicable to administration of the city sales tax as
if here set forth in full.
(1999 Code, § 37.33) (Ord. 11, passed 3-18-1969; Ord. 32, passed 7-7-1977; Ord.
passed 4-7-2007; Ord. passed 3-12-2009)
USE TAX
§ 37.45 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known and may be cited as “The City of Hooker Use
Tax Ordinance”.
(1999 Code, § 37.45) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.46 PURPOSE.
   It is hereby declared to be the purpose of this subchapter to provide
revenues for the support of the functions of the municipal government of the
municipality, and any and all revenues derived hereunder may be expended by the
governing body of the municipality for any purpose for which funds may be
lawfully expended as authorized.
(1999 Code, § 37.46) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.47 EFFECT ON OTHER TAXES.
   The provisions hereof shall be cumulative and in addition to any and all
other taxing provisions of city ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 37.47) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.48 EFFECT ON EXISTING STATE PERMITS.
   All valid and subsisting permits to do business issued by the Tax Commission
pursuant to the State Use Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq. are for
the purpose of this subchapter hereby ratified, confirmed and adopted in lieu
of any requirement for an additional city permit for the same purpose.
(1999 Code, § 37.48) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.49 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   The definitions of words, terms and phrases contained in the State Use
Tax Code, 68 O.S. § 1401 are hereby adopted by reference and made a part of
this subchapter.
   (B)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      TAX COLLECTOR. The department of the city government or the official
agency of the state, duly designated, according to law or contract authorized
by law, to administer the collection of the tax herein levied.
      TRANSACTION. Sale.
(1999 Code, § 37.49) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.50 TAX RATE; TAXABLE EVENTS.
   There is hereby levied and there shall be paid by every person storing,
using or otherwise consuming within the municipality tangible, personal
property purchased or brought into this municipality an excise tax on the
storage, use or other consuming within the municipality of such property at the
rate of 2% of the purchase price of such property. Such tax shall paid by every
person storing, using or otherwise consuming within the municipality tangible,
personal property purchased or brought into the municipality. The additional
tax levied hereunder shall be paid at the time of importation or storage of the
property within the municipality and shall be assessed to only property
purchased outside the state; provided that the tax levied herein shall not be
levied against tangible, personal property intended solely for use outside the
municipality, but which is stored in the municipality pending shipment outside
the municipality or which is temporarily retained in the municipality for the
purpose of fabrication, repair, testing, alteration, maintenance or other
service. Any person liable for payment of the tax authorized herein may deduct
from such tax any local municipal sales tax previously paid on such goods or
services, provided that the amount deducted shall not exceed the amount that
would have been due if the taxes imposed by the municipality had been levied on
the sale of such goods or services.
(1999 Code, § 37.50) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.51 EXEMPTIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply:
   (A)   In respect to the use of an article of tangible, personal property
brought into the municipality by a nonresident individual visiting in this
municipality for his or her personal use or enjoyment while within the
municipality;
   (B)   In respect to the use of tangible, personal property purchased for
resale before being used;
   (C)   In respect to the use of any article of tangible, personal property on
which a tax, equal to or in excess of that levied by both the State Use Tax
Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq. and the city use tax regulations, has
been paid by the person using such tangible, personal property in the
municipality, whether such tax was levied under the laws of this state or some
other state or municipality of the United States. If any article of tangible,
personal property has already been subjected to a tax by this state or any
other state or municipality in respect to its sale or use in an amount less
than the tax imposed by both the State Use Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14
et seq. and the city use tax regulations, the provisions of this subchapter
shall also apply to it by a rate measured by the difference only between the
rate provided by both the State Use Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq.
and the city use tax regulations, and the rate by which the previous tax upon
the sale or use was computed, provided that no credit shall be given for taxes
paid in another state or municipality if that state or municipality does not
grant like credit for taxes paid in the state and the municipality;
   (D)   In respect to the use of machinery and equipment purchased and used by
persons establishing new manufacturing or processing plants in the
municipality, and machinery and equipment purchased and used by persons in the
operation of manufacturing plants already established in the municipality,
provided that this exemption shall not apply unless such machinery and
equipment is incorporated into, and is directly used in, the process of
manufacturing property subject to taxation under the Sales Tax Code of the
municipality. The term MANUFACTURING PLANTS shall mean those establishments
primarily engaged in manufacturing or processing operations, and generally
recognized as such;
   (E)   In respect to the use of tangible, personal property now specifically
exempted from taxation under the Sales Tax Code of the municipality;
   (F)   In respect to the use of any article of tangible, personal property
brought into the municipality by an individual with intent to become a resident
of this municipality where such personal property is for such individual’s
personal use or enjoyment;
   (G)   In respect to the use of any article of tangible personal property
used or to be used by commercial airlines or railroads; and
   (H)   In respect to livestock purchased outside the state and brought into
this municipality for feeding or breeding purposes, and which is later resold.
(1999 Code, § 37.51) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.52 PAYMENT OF TAX.
   The tax levied by this subchapter is due and payable at the time and in the
manner and form prescribed for payment of the state use tax under the State Use
Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq.
(1999 Code, § 37.52) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.53 TAX AS DEBT; TAX PRIORITY.
   Such taxes, penalty and interest due hereunder shall at all times constitute
a prior, superior and paramount claim as against the claims of unsecured
creditors, and may be collected by suit as any other debt.
(1999 Code, § 37.53) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.54 CLASSIFICATION OF TAXPAYERS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the classification of taxpayers
hereunder shall be as prescribed by state law for purposes of the State Use Tax
Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq.
(1999 Code, § 37.54) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.55 COLLECTION OF TAX BY RETAILER OR VENDOR; PERMITS.
   (A)   Collection of tax by retailer or vendor generally. Every retailer or
vendor maintaining places of business both within and without this state and
making sales of tangible, personal property from a place of business outside
this state for use in this municipality shall at the time of making such sales
collect the use tax levied by this subchapter from the purchaser and give to
the purchaser a receipt therefor in the manner and form prescribed by the Tax
Commission, if the Tax Commission shall, by regulation, require such receipt.
Each retailer or vendor shall list with the Tax Commission the name and address
of all his or her agents operating in this municipality and the location of any
and all distribution or sales houses or offices or other places of business in
this city.
   (B)   Collection of tax by retailer or vendor not maintaining a place of
business within this state or both within and without the state; permits. The
Tax Commission may, in its discretion, upon application, authorize the
collection of the tax herein levied by any retailer or vendor not maintaining a
place of business within this state but who makes sales of tangible personal
property for use in this municipality and by the out of state place of business
of any retailer or vendor maintaining places of business both within and
without the state and making sales of tangible, personal property at such out
of state place of business for use in this municipality. Such retailer or
vendor may be issued, without charge, a permit to collect such taxes by the Tax
Commission in such manner and subject to such regulations and agreements as it
shall prescribe. When so authorized, it shall be the duty of such retailer or
vendor to collect the tax upon all tangible, personal property sold to his or
her knowledge for use within this municipality. Such authority and permit may
be cancelled when at any time the Tax Commission considers that such tax can
more effectively be collected from the person using such property in this
municipality; provided, however, that in all instances where such sales are
made or completed by delivery to the purchaser within this municipality by the
retailer or vendor in such retailer’s or vendor’s vehicle, whether owned or
leased (not by common carrier), such sales or transactions shall continue to be
subject to applicable municipality sales tax at the point of delivery, and the
tax shall be collected and reported under the taxpayer’s sales tax permit
number accordingly.
(1999 Code, § 37.55) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.56 PERMIT REVOCATION.
   Whenever any retailer or vendor not maintaining a place of business in this
state, or whenever any retailer or vendor maintaining a place of business both
within and without this state, and authorized to collect the tax herein levied,
fails to comply with any of the provisions of this subchapter or the State Use
Tax Code, being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq. or any order, rules or regulations
of the Tax Commission, the Tax Commission may, upon notice and hearing as
provided for in 68 O.S. § 1408, by order revoke the use tax permit, if any,
issued to such retailer or vendor, and if any such retailer or vendor is a
corporation authorized to do business in this state may, after notice and
hearing above provided, cancel said corporation’s license to do business in
this state and shall issue a new license only when such corporation has
complied with the obligations under this subchapter, the State Use Tax Code,
being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq. or any order, rules or regulations of the Tax
Commission.
(1999 Code, § 37.56) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.57 RETURNS AND REMITTANCES; DISCOUNT.
   Returns and remittances of the tax herein levied and collected shall be made
to the Tax Commission at the time and in the manner, form and amount as
prescribed for returns and remittances required by the State Use Tax Code,
being 68 O.S. §§ 1354.14 et seq., and remittances of tax collected hereunder
shall be subject to the same discount as may be allowed by said code for the
collection of state use taxes.
(1999 Code, § 37.57) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.58 INTEREST AND PENALTIES.
   (A)   Delinquency. 68 O.S. § 217 is hereby adopted and made a part of this
subchapter, and interest and penalties at the rates and in the amounts as
therein specified are hereby levied and shall be applicable in cases of
delinquency in reporting and paying the tax levied by this subchapter, provided
that the failure or refusal of any retailer or vendor to make and transmit the
reports and remittances of tax in the time and manner required by this
subchapter shall cause such tax to be delinquent. In addition, if such
delinquency continues for a period of five days, the retailer or vendor shall
forfeit his or her claim to any discount allowed under this subchapter.
   (B)   Waiver of interest and penalties. The interest or penalty or any
portion thereof accruing by reason of a retailer’s or vendor’s failure to pay
the municipality tax herein levied may be waived or remitted in the same manner
as provided for said waiver or remittance as applied in administration of the
state use tax provided in 68 O.S. § 220, and to accomplish the purposes of this
section the applicable provisions of said § 220 are hereby adopted by reference
and made a part of this subchapter.
(1999 Code, § 37.58) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.59 ERRONEOUS PAYMENTS; CLAIM FOR REFUND.
   Refund of erroneous payment of the municipality use tax herein levied may be
made to any taxpayer making such erroneous payment in the same manner and
procedure, and under the same limitations of time, as provided for
administration of the state use tax as set forth in 68 O.S. § 227, and to
accomplish the purpose of this section, the applicable provisions of said § 227
are hereby adopted by reference and made a part of this subchapter.
(1999 Code, § 37.59) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
§ 37.60 FALSE RETURNS.
   In addition to all civil penalties provided by this subchapter, the willful
failure or refusal of any taxpayer to make reports and remittances herein
required, or the making of any false and fraudulent report for the purpose of
avoiding or escaping payment of any tax or portion thereof rightfully due under
this subchapter, shall be an offense, and upon conviction thereof the offending
taxpayer shall be punished as provided in §
10.99.
(1999 Code, § 37.60) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007) Penalty,
see §
10.99
§ 37.61 RECORD CONFIDENTIALITY.
   The confidential and privileged nature of the records and files concerning
the administration of the municipality use tax is legislatively recognized and
declared, and to protect the same the provisions of 68 O.S. § 205, of the State
Use Tax Code, and each division thereof, are hereby adopted by reference and
made fully effective and applicable to administration of the municipality use
tax as is herein set forth in full.
(1999 Code, § 37.61) (Ord. 89, passed 2-3-1992; Ord. passed 4-12-2007)
CHAPTER 38: PERSONNEL POLICIES
Section
   
38.01   Appointment of personnel
   
38.02   Removal of officers and employees
   
38.03   Bond of officers and employees
   
38.04   Compensation
   
38.05   Old Age, Survivors’ and Disability Insurance
   
38.06   Retirement plan
§ 38.01 APPOINTMENT OF PERSONNEL.
   The Mayor, with approval of the Council, shall appoint such water,
sanitation, cemetery and other personnel as may be necessary to exercise the
powers and perform the duties relative to the functions which are lawfully
imposed upon or assumed by the city.
(1999 Code, § 38.01)
§ 38.02 REMOVAL OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES.
   Except as may be otherwise provided by law, officers and employees of the
city who are appointed by the Mayor with approval of the Council may be
removed, suspended or laid off by the Mayor with approval of the Council.
(1999 Code, § 38.02)
§ 38.03 BOND OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES.
   (A)   Before entering upon their official duties, the following personnel of
the city government shall provide bonds for the faithful performance of their
official duties, payable to the city, with a surety company authorized to
operate within the state, in the amounts respectively indicated after their
titles:
      (1)   City Clerk, $28,000;
      (2)   City Treasurer, $28,000; and
      (3)   Chief of Police, $28,000.
   (B)   The Council, by motion or resolution, may require other officers and
employees in such positions as it may designate to be bonded; also by motion or
resolution may increase the amount of the bonds for the personnel listed in
division (A) above; and also may provide for blanket bonds for city personnel.
   (C)   The city shall pay the premiums on such bonds.
(1999 Code, § 38.03)
§ 38.04 COMPENSATION.
   The Council by motion or resolution may fix the compensation of personnel
other than the compensation of the Mayor, Council members, City Clerk and City
Treasurer, which shall be fixed by ordinance.
(1999 Code, § 38.04) (Ord. 57, passed 1-3-1983)
§ 38.05 OLD AGE, SURVIVORS’ AND DISABILITY INSURANCE.
   (A)   Benefits of federal O.A.S.D.I. to be extended to personnel. It is
hereby declared to be the policy and purpose of the city to extend, at the
earliest date, to the employees and officials thereof, not excluded by law or
ordinance, and whether employed in connection with a governmental or
proprietary function, the benefits of the system of Federal Old Age, Survivors’
and Disability Insurance as authorized by the Federal Social Security Act and
amendments thereto, including Public Law 734, 81st Congress, being codified at
42 U.S.C. §§ 301 et seq. In pursuance of said policy, and for that purpose, the
city shall take such action as may be required by applicable state or federal
laws or regulations.
   (B)   Mayor authorized to execute agreements. The Mayor of the city is
hereby authorized and directed to execute all necessary agreements and
amendments according to state the federal laws, to secure coverage of employees
and officials as provided in division (A) above.
   (C)   Withholdings from salaries and wages. Withholdings from salaries or
wages of employees and officials for the purpose in division (A) above are
hereby authorized to be made in the amounts and at such times as may be
required by applicable state or federal laws or regulations and shall be paid
over to the state or federal agency designated by said laws or regulations.
   (D)   Appropriations for employer’s contributions. There shall be
appropriated from available funds such amounts at such times as may be required
by applicable state or federal laws or regulations for employer’s
contributions, which shall be paid over to the state or federal agency
designated by said laws or regulations.
   (E)   Records and reports. The city shall keep such records and make such
reports as may be required by applicable state or federal laws or regulations.
   (F)   Employees and officers now covered by other retirement systems. There
is hereby excluded from this section any authority to make any agreement with
respect to any position or any employee or official now covered or authorized
to be covered by any other ordinance creating any retirement system for any
employee or official of the city.
   (G)   Employees and officers on a fee basis excluded and the like. There is
hereby excluded from this section any authority to make any agreement with
respect to any position or any employee or official whose compensation is on a
fee basis, or any position or any employee or official not authorized to be
covered by applicable state or federal laws or regulations.
(1999 Code, § 38.05)
§ 38.06 RETIREMENT PLAN.
   The retirement plan of the city as adopted by Ord. 105 on August 7, 1995, as
amended, is hereby incorporated by reference as if set out in full herein.
(1999 Code, § 38.06) (Ord. 105, passed 8-7-1995; Ord. 109, passed 4-8-1996;
Ord. 130, passed 6-21-2001; Ord. 135, passed 7-6-2006; Ord. 2007-10, passed 6-
14-2007; Ord. 2008-6, passed 10-6-2008; Ord. 2010-7, passed 12-6-2010; Ord.
2014-2, passed 11-3-2014; Ord. 2020-02, passed 1-7-2020; Ord. 2020-5, passed 6-
15-2020)
CHAPTER 39: ELECTIONS
Section
   
39.01   General election
   
39.02   Primary election
   
39.03   Elections to be held by Election Board of the county
§ 39.01 GENERAL ELECTION.
   A general election shall be held in the city on the first Tuesday in April
of every odd-numbered year to elect the following city officers:
   (A)   Mayor;
   (B)   City Clerk;
   (C)   City Treasurer; and
   (D)   One Council member from each ward of the city.
(1999 Code, § 39.01)
§ 39.02 PRIMARY ELECTION.
   On the third Tuesday in March of every odd-numbered year (just prior to the
general election), a primary election shall be held to nominate candidates for
the offices set forth in §
39.01.
(1999 Code, § 39.02)
§ 39.03 ELECTIONS TO BE HELD BY ELECTION BOARD OF THE COUNTY.
   (A)   For the purpose of municipal elections, the municipal officials
approve the County Election Board holding the city’s elections.
   (B)   The County Election Board has in the past held the nonpartisan general
elections for the city and to comply with state law concerning elections, the
city hereby approves and directs the County Election Board to hold elections
for the city for the offices of Mayor, Treasurer, City Clerk and four Council
members.
   (C)   The officers of the city to be elected are nominated by ward and
elected at large and will be elected for four-year terms with the elections
being held on odd years.
   (D)   Each candidate must be a qualified elector by virtue of being a
resident and registered voter within the municipality and in the ward for
offices from wards for at least six months prior to filing a declaration of
candidacy.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 1-8-2015)
CHAPTER 40: EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT
Section
   
40.01   Purpose
   
40.02   Establishment of Emergency Management Department, Director and
Committee
   
40.03   Director; powers and duties
   
40.04   Plan and records
   
40.05   Emergencies
   
40.06   Law enforcement and arrest powers
   
40.07   Compensation; liability of city
§ 40.01 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to update and to change the name of the civil
defense organization for the city. The same organization shall now be the
Emergency Management Department as was and is designed to be prepared for, and
to function in the event of emergencies endangering the lives and property of
the people of the city. The duty of the emergency management organization shall
be the protection of the lives and health of the citizens of the city and of
property and property rights, both private and public, and to perform all
functions necessary and incident thereto.
(1999 Code, § 40.01) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.02 ESTABLISHMENT OF EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT DEPARTMENT, DIRECTOR AND
COMMITTEE.
   There is hereby established under the executive branch of the government of
the city the Department of Emergency Management which shall consist of:
   (A)   A Director of Emergency Management who shall be appointed by the Mayor
of the city and serve at his or her pleasure;
   (B)   A Co-Director of Emergency Management who shall be appointed by the
Mayor of the city and assist the Director whether it be one or the other who
serves in the capacity when one is absent and together in different positions
when both are functioning in the capacity of an emergency, and who serves the
Mayor when needed; and
   (C)   An Emergency Management Committee or members of the trained disaster
plan preparedness shall be appointed by the Mayor and serve at his or her
pleasure; the duty of the Committee to help the Director and/or Co-Director of
Emergency Management.
(1999 Code, § 40.02) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.03 DIRECTOR; POWERS AND DUTIES.
   The Director and Co-Director of Emergency Management shall be the executive
heads and will be responsible for carrying out the emergency management plan or
program of the city. The Co-Director will be responsible for the training of
personnel set forth by federal and state requirements through the National
Incident Management System (NIMS). They shall serve without compensation but
may be reimbursed for expenses incurred in the performance of his or her
duties. It is the duty of the Director and Co-Director to carry out the
purposes set forth in this chapter and shall have all necessary power and
authority to form committees or other bodies to carry out their
responsibilities.
(1999 Code, § 40.03) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.04 PLAN AND RECORDS.
   The Director and Co-Director is further authorized to formulate written
plans and gather information and keep written records thereof to govern the
functions of the emergency management.
(1999 Code, § 40.04) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.05 EMERGENCIES.
   In the event of a terrorist or enemy-caused emergency or natural disaster,
the Directors, after due authorization from the Mayor of the city, shall have
the power and authority to enforce all rules and regulations relating to
emergency management, and, if necessary, take control of transportation,
communications, stocks of fuel, food, clothing, medicine and public utilities
for the purpose of protecting the civilian population. They shall cooperate
with the activities of other governmental agencies; FEMA; Homeland Security;
and OEMS, including other local emergency management directors or committees.
If required by the Mayor, the Directors shall have control over any and all
funds allocated from any source for the purpose of alleviating distress
conditions in the city.
(1999 Code, § 40.05) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.06 LAW ENFORCEMENT AND ARREST POWERS.
   Directors of Emergency Management or members of the city’s emergency
response personnel shall have the power and authority to enforce the laws of
the state and ordinances of the city during the period of emergency or disaster
and shall at such time have the further power to make arrests for violations of
such laws or ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 40.06) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
§ 40.07 COMPENSATION; LIABILITY OF CITY.
   All members of the emergency management team and/or organization created
hereunder shall serve without compensation, and the city shall not be liable
for any personal injury received by any member of the emergency management team
while acting in the line of duty.
(1999 Code, § 40.07) (Ord. 2011-2, passed 7-7-2011)
CHAPTER 41: CITY POLICY
Section
   
41.01   Smoking policy
§ 41.01 SMOKING POLICY.
   (A)   Smoking has been shown to be responsible for much illness and early
death. Smoke-laden air (passive smoke) also affects the non-smoker’s health and
causes discomfort.
   (B)   Therefore, in an effort to provide a pleasant environment for all of
our patrons and employees while recognizing the preferences of smokers, the
following smoking policy is adopted by this municipality.
      (1)   This entire municipal facility is designated as non-smoking.
Smoking shall not be allowed in any area. All entrances to the facility are
posted with signs stating that “SMOKING IS PROHIBITED”. All employees and
patrons are requested to honor the non-smoking designation and to respect the
preferences of others.
      (2)   Management bears the responsibility for addressing complaints,
including asking smokers to refrain from smoking upon request of a patron or
employee suffering discomfort from smoke or who has hypersensitivity to smoke.
(1999 Code, § 41.01) (Res. passed 12-5-1994)

CHAPTER 50: GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section
   
50.01   Utility deposits
§ 50.01 UTILITY DEPOSITS.
   Effective upon adoption of this section, money in the Municipal Treasury
which has been acquired as a utility deposit from a customer of a municipal
utility shall be refunded or credited to the customer upon termination of the
utility service and payment of all charges due and connected with the service,
or at an earlier date as may be allowed by the municipality. If the deposit has
not been claimed by or refunded to a customer within one year following
termination of the utility service to the customer, the municipality shall send
written notice to the customer at his or her last known address stating that
the deposit will be paid over to the municipality unless it is claimed by the
customer within 90 days of the date the notice is mailed by the municipality.
If the money is not claimed or refunded within the 90 days, the amount of the
deposit shall be paid into the fund of the municipal utility for which the
deposit was collected, or into the General Fund as may be determined by the
City Council. No municipal utility customer shall have a right to any claim or
refund on the deposit after written notice and expiration of the 90-day period
in accordance with this section.
(1999 Code, § 50.01) (Ord. 66, passed 11-7-1983)
Cross-reference:
   Sewer; fees and deposits, see §
53.03
   Water; fees and deposits, see §
52.03
CHAPTER 51: SOLID WASTE
Section
Collection of Garbage and Trash

COLLECTION OF GARBAGE AND TRASH
§ 51.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   GARBAGE. Vegetable or animal refuse accumulating from homes, hotels, motels,
restaurants, dwellings, markets, stores and other establishments.
   TRASH. Any refuse, litter, ashes, leaves, debris, paper, combustible
materials, rubbish, offal or waste, or matter of any kind or form which is
uncared for, discarded or abandoned.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019)
§ 51.02 UNLAWFUL TO ALLOW GARBAGE AND TRASH TO ACCUMULATE.
   It is unlawful for the owner or occupants of any premises in the city to
allow garbage and trash, or either of them, to suffer or permit water or putrid
substances, whether vegetable or animal to accumulate thereon so as to cause an
offensive odor to be emitted, or to become in any condition injurious or
dangerous to the health of the neighborhood or any inhabitant thereof. Any such
condition is hereby declared to be in violation of this subchapter, and in
addition, is declared to be a nuisance and may be abated as such.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.03 GARBAGE CONTAINERS.
   Except as provided in §
51.04, the owners or occupants of all residences and business premises in the
city shall place all garbage and trash in steel bins as provided by the city
and placed at strategic locations throughout the city.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019)
§ 51.04 CUSTOMER SERVICE WITHIN THREE-MILE RADIUS OF THE CITY LIMITS.
   The city shall place garbage bins as provided to the city residences and
businesses within a three- mile radius of the city limits at the request of
occupants of residences within said area; with the same regulations as listed
herein.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019)
§ 51.05 PROHIBITED MATERIAL AND DISPOSAL.
   The following described materials and materials of the same class are
prohibited materials and shall not be placed in or beside the steel trash bins:
   (A)   Dirt, sand, gravel, cement or manure;
   (B)   Masonry, masonry products, building materials, wood, shingles, lumber,
floor coverings, carpet, pallets, metal, construction components, construction
or remodeling debris;
   (C)   Machinery, equipment, appliances, furniture, tires or other motor
vehicle parts;
   (D)   Grass, shrub trimmings, trees, tree limbs, tree stumps, leaves or
other yard waste;
   (E)   Hazardous or flammable material;
   (F)   Business or industrial waste; and
   (G)   Other material of like size, density or mass, which because of its
nature is likely to damage city owned equipment or injure city personnel.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.06 REMOVAL BY CITY OR BY CONTRACT AND THE LIKE.
   (A) Generally. The city shall have the exclusive right to collect, remove
and dispose of garbage and trash, or either of them, in the city and within the
three-mile radius, or may, through its duly elected, qualified and acting
officers, enter into a contract with some suitable person, firm or corporation
granting the exclusive right to collect, remove and dispose of garbage and
trash, or either of them, in regards to the city.
   (B)   Only authorized persons to transport garbage and trash. It is unlawful
for any person, firm or corporation, unless authorized to do so by the city, to
remove from any premises situated in the city or the city’s area of service to
transport through the streets, alleys or public places of the city any garbage
or trash.
   (C)   Fees.
      (1)   Generally.
         (a)   The owners or occupants of all such residences, business
premises, churches and schools shall pay reasonable fees for the removal of
garbage and trash, or either of them, whether removed by the city or by
contractor, the amount of such fees to be determined by the Mayor and City
Council. Such fees shall be collected monthly at the office of the City Clerk
in the same manner and at the same time as bills for water are rendered and
collected. To all bills or charges for such services not paid by the tenth day
of the month, a penalty of 10% per month shall be added.
         (b)   The fees for collection and removal of garbage and trash shall
be as follows:
            1.   In residences occupied by only one family, the family shall
pay $28 per month:
            2.   In duplexes, apartment houses and all other buildings where
more than one family reside or board, each family shall pay $28 per month;
            3.   In all other buildings where no more than one family resides
or boards, the charge shall be the amount determined by the Mayor and City
Council, but not to exceed $28 per family;
            4.   All schools and business places shall be charged a minimum of
$38 per month with a charge of $38 for each additional trash receptacle at
their place of service or business;
            5.   Any business sharing a single dwelling will be sent one bill
and charged one water rate of $26; one sewer rate of $15 and two base trash
rates consisting of one business rate for $38 and one residential rate for $28
totaling $66 per month;
            6.   All churches and charitable organizations shall receive a
charge for their trash collection of $28 per month;
            7.   All businesses at residences shall have a charge of $8 for
their business trash collection and $28 for their residence trash collection,
making their monthly charge $36. The provision of adequate trash receptacles at
the businesses shall be the duty of the city;
            8.   Residences who are outside the city limits shall receive a
charge of $38 per month; and
            9.   Three thousand five hundred dollars of all gross receipts for
collection of water, sewer and garbage shall be set aside in the Capital
Improvement Garbage Fund and $5,000 of all gross receipts for collection of
water, sewer and garbage shall be set aside in a Capital Improvement Fund as
designated by motion of the City Council.
      (2)   Roll-off bins. For the purpose of providing funds to provide
service and personnel and use of the city roll-off bin located at any location
by choice of the city, and for the convenience of citizens to have a receptacle
to dispose of approved items outside the criteria of allowable dumpster items,
there is hereby established a schedule of fees and charges:
         (a)   For any disposal, a minimum $5 fee will be charged at the time
of disposal;
         (b)   For disposals of pick-up size loads, a minimum $10 fee will be
charged at the time of disposal; and
         (c)   For larger or trailer size disposals, a minimum $20 fee will be
charged at the time of disposal.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2015-2, passed 6-4-2015; Ord. 2019-3,
passed 6-13-2019)
§ 51.07 UNLAWFUL USE OF THE CITY TRASH RECEPTACLES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation who does not pay
trash collection fees to the city to place any material in any trash bin or
receptacle.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.08 SANITARY INSPECTOR.
   (A)   The Mayor of the city shall appoint a Sanitary Inspector, who shall be
appointed as a member of the City Police Department.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of the Sanitary Inspector to inspect all premises
in the city as often as may be required, and to report any and all unsanitary
conditions to the Mayor and Council and to the owner or occupant of the
premises where such conditions are found.
   (C)   It shall be the further duty of the Sanitary Inspector to make written
reports covering the sanitary conditions in the city.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019)
§ 51.09 BURNING REFUSE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to burn any
combustible refuse or garbage within the city limits of the city.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.10 USE OF CITY’S LANDFILL GROUNDS.
   (A)   Generally. No person, resident or nonresident of the city shall
deposit any trash, garbage, carcass, car body, concrete or any other solid
waste material upon the city landfill grounds without first obtaining
permission from the City Superintendent.
   (B)   Unlawful hauling and dumping; presumptions.
      (1)   Prima facie presumption that a registered owner of a vehicle
committed a violation. In any prosecution charging a violation of division (A)
above, proof that a particular vehicle described in the complaint was used for
the purpose of unlawfully hauling or dumping of refuse matter as prohibited
therein together with proof that the individual named in the complaint was at
the time of violation the registered owner of said vehicle shall constitute in
evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered owner of said vehicle
was the person who committed the violation.
      (2)   Prima facie presumption that a person whose address appears on
three or more items of unlawfully disposed of refuse matter committed a
violation of division (A) above. Proof that unlawfully disposed of refuse
matter as described therein which contains three or more items bearing a common
address in a form which tends to identify the latest owner of the items shall
be a prima facie presumption that all competent persons residing at such
address committed the unlawful act of disposal provided that one of the said
items of solid waste bears a date subsequent to October 3, 1994.
      (3)   Allowing refuse to be deposited or remain on premises. No owner or
occupant of land or lots shall knowingly permit the throwing or dumping upon
his or her premises of the material described in division (A) above or permit
these materials to remain on his or her premises after being notified to remove
them by the offices of the city, whether he or she shall have known of or
permitted the throwing or depositing or not.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter, for which no other
penalty is provided, shall be subject to the penalty provisions of §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person, firm, co-partnership, corporation, club or society who
violates, disobeys or omits, neglects or refuses to comply with any provision
of §§
51.01 through
51.10 shall be guilty of an offense, and shall, upon conviction, be punished by
a fine not to exceed $500 or imprisonment not to exceed 60 days or both fine
and imprisonment.
(Ord. 2007-11, passed 7-17-2007; Ord. 2019-3, passed 6-13-2019)
