GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 96.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   NUISANCE. Unlawfully doing an act, or omitting to perform a duty or any
thing or condition which either:
      (1)   Annoys, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health or safety
of others;
      (2)   Offends decency;
      (3)   Unlawfully interferes with, obstructs or tends to obstruct, or
renders dangerous for passage, any lake or navigable river, stream, canal or
basin or any public park, square, street or other public property; or
      (4)   In any way renders other persons insecure in life or in the use of
property.
   NUISANCE, PRIVATE. Every nuisance not a public nuisance is a PRIVATE
NUISANCE.
   NUISANCE, PUBLIC. A nuisance which affects at the same time an entire
community or neighborhood or any considerable number of persons, although the
extent of the annoyance or damage inflicted upon the individuals may be
unequal.
(50 O.S. §§ 1 through 3) (1999 Code, § 96.01)
§ 96.002 AUTHORITY OF CITY.
   As provided in 50 O.S. § 16, the city has power to determine what is and
what shall constitute a nuisance within its corporate limits and, for the
protection of the public health, the public parks and the public water supply,
outside of its corporate limits. Whenever it is practical to do so, the city
has power summarily to abate any such nuisance after notice to the owner and an
opportunity for him or her to be heard, if this can be done.
(50 O.S. § 16) (1999 Code, § 96.02)
§ 96.003 PUBLIC NUISANCES DEFINED.
   (A)   In addition to other public nuisances declared by other sections of
this title, the following are hereby declared to be public nuisances:
      (1)   The sale, or offering for sale, of unwholesome food or drink; or
the keeping of a place hereby declared to be public nuisances;
      (2)   The sale, offering for sale or furnishing of intoxicating liquor in
violation of the state law or ordinances of the city; or keeping of a place
where intoxicating liquor is sold, offered for sale or furnished in violation
of the state law or ordinances of the city;
      (3)   The exposure, display, sale or distribution of obscene pictures,
books, pamphlets, magazines, papers, documents or objects; or the keeping of a
place where such are exposed, displayed, sold or distributed;
      (4)   The keeping of a place where prostitution, illicit sexual
intercourse or other immoral acts are practiced;
      (5)   The keeping of a place where activities in violation of state law
or ordinance are practiced;
      (6)   The public exposure of a person having a contagious disease;
      (7)   Carrying on or conducting any business, trade, manufacturing,
employment or other activity which causes noxious, injurious or offensive odors
or fumes; or which emits or causes or is accompanied by loud, annoying or
offensive language or noises; or which is injurious or dangerous to the health
or safety of others, or which creates a public health or safety hazard;
      (8)   The continued making of loud or unusual noises which annoy persons
of ordinary sensibilities; or the keeping of an animal that makes such noises;
      (9)   The operation or use of any electrical apparatus or machine which
materially and unduly interferes with radio or television reception of others;
      (10)   Any use of a street or sidewalk or a place adjacent thereto which
causes crowds of people to gather so as to obstruct traffic on such street or
sidewalk, or which otherwise obstructs traffic thereon, except as may be
authorized by law or ordinance;
      (11)   Permitting water or other liquid to flow or fall, or ice or snow
to fall, from any building or structure upon any street or sidewalk;
      (12)   All wells, pools, cisterns, bodies or containers or water in which
mosquitoes breed or are likely to breed;
      (13)   Rank weeds or grass, carcasses, accumulations of manure, refuse or
other things, which are, or are likely to be, breeding places for flies,
mosquitoes, vermin or disease germs;
      (14)   Any building or structure that is dangerous to the public health
or safety because of damage, decay or other condition;
      (15)   Any pit, hole or other thing which is constructed, formed,
conditioned and/or situated as to endanger the public safety;
      (16)   Any fire or explosion hazard which endangers the public safety;
      (17)   Any occupation or activity which endangers the public peace,
health, safety, morals or welfare; and
      (18)   GRAFFITI is defined as the unauthorized spraying of paint or
marking of ink, chalk, dye or other similar substances on public and private
buildings, structures and places. The existence of graffiti or the act of
placing graffiti on any real or personal property, of altering or defacing any
real or personal property of another without their consent through the use of
paint, spray paint, markers, objects or other substances capable of destroying
property which is offensive to a reasonably sensitive person. The following
acts are prohibited:
         (a)   To apply graffiti upon any surface, either publicly or privately
owned, without the permission of the owner, lessee or person in legal
possession;
         (b)   To have graffiti on property which can be seen from the public
right-of-way;
         (c)   To have graffiti on property which can be seen from private
property upon which a complaint has been made; or
         (d)   To have graffiti on property which causes a depreciation of the
property values or is detrimental to neighborhoods.
   (B)   Any of the above acts shall constitute a public nuisance and shall be
abated as set out in this code of ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 96.03) (Ord. 2010-8, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.004 NUISANCES PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful for any person (owner, lessee or other) to create or maintain
a nuisance within the city, or to permit a nuisance to remain on premises under
his or her control within the city.
(1999 Code, § 96.04) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.005 LIABILITY FOR NUISANCES.
   Every successive owner of property who neglects to abate a continuing
nuisance upon or in the use of such property created by a former owner is
liable therefor in the same manner as the one who first created it.
(1999 Code, § 96.05)
§ 96.006 TIME PASSAGE DOES NOT LEGALIZE NUISANCE.
   No lapse of time can legalize a public nuisance amounting to an actual
obstruction of a public right.
(50 O.S. § 7) (1999 Code, § 96.06)
§ 96.007 REMEDIES AGAINST PUBLIC NUISANCE.
   The remedies against public nuisances are:
   (A)   Prosecution on complaint before the Municipal Court;
   (B)   Prosecution on information or indictment before another appropriate
court;
   (C)   Civil action; and
   (D)   Abatement:
      (1)   By a person injured as provided in 50 O.S. § 12; or
      (2)   By the city in accordance with law or ordinance.
(50 O.S. § 8) (1999 Code, § 96.07)
§ 96.008 REMEDIES AGAINST PRIVATE NUISANCE.
   The remedies against a private nuisance are:
   (A)   Civil action; and
   (B)   Abatement:
      (1)   By person injured as provided in 50 O.S. §§ 14 and 15; or
      (2)   By the city in accordance with law or ordinance.
(1999 Code, § 96.08)
§ 96.009 SUMMARY ABATEMENT.
   (A)   Some nuisances are of such nature as to constitute a grave and
immediate danger to the peace, health, safety, morals or welfare of one or more
persons or of the public generally. It is recognized that circumstances may be
such as to justify and even to require the Mayor or other appropriate officer
or agency of the city government to take immediate and proper action summarily
to abate such nuisances, or to reduce or suspend the danger until more
deliberate action can be taken toward such abatement.
   (B)   The Chief of the Fire Department, the Chief of Police, the City
Attorney, the Building Inspector, the Electrical Inspector, the Plumbing
Inspector or any other officer subordinate to the Mayor may submit, through or
with the consent of the Mayor to the City Council, a statement as to the
existence of a nuisance as defined by the ordinances of the city or law, and a
request or recommendation that it be abated. The Mayor himself or herself, the
Health Officer, any Council member, or any resident or residents of the city
may submit such a statement and request or recommendation to the City Council.
   (C)   The Council shall determine whether or not the alleged nuisance is a
nuisance in fact. For the purpose of gathering evidence on the subject, the
Council shall have power to subpoena and examine witnesses, books, papers and
other effects. Before proceeding to abate the nuisance or have it abated, the
Council shall give notice of a hearing on the proposed abatement to the owner
of any property concerned and to any other person alleged or deemed responsible
for or to be causing the nuisance and an adequate opportunity to be heard, if
such notice and opportunity for a hearing can be given. Such notice to the
owner and other persons concerned shall be given in writing by mail or by
service by a police officer if their names and addresses are known, but, if the
names or addresses are not known and the peace, health, safety, morals or
welfare of the person or persons or public adversely affected would not be
unduly jeopardized by the necessary delay, a notice of the hearing shall be
published in a paper of general circulation within the city.
   (D)   If the Council finds that a nuisance does in fact exist, it shall
direct the owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing the nuisance
to abate it within a specified time if the peace, health, safety, morals or
welfare of the person or persons or public adversely affected would not be
unduly jeopardized by the consequent delay. If such peace, health, safety,
morals or welfare would be unduly jeopardized by the consequent delay, or if
the owner or other persons responsible for or causing the nuisance do not abate
it within the specified time, the Council shall direct the Mayor to abate the
nuisance or to have it abated, if summary abatement is practical, as authorized
by 50 O.S. § 16. The City Clerk shall send a statement of the cost of such
summary abatement to the owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing
the nuisance as may be just under the circumstances, if their names and
addresses are known. Until paid, such cost shall constitute a debt to the city
collectible as other debts of the city may be collected.
(1999 Code, § 96.09)
§ 96.010 ABATEMENT BY CITY LAWSUIT.
   In cases where it is deemed impractical summarily to abate a nuisance, the
city may bring suit in the District Court of the county where the nuisance is
located, as provided in 50 O.S. § 17.
(1999 Code, § 96.10)
§ 96.011 ABATEMENT PROCEDURES CUMULATIVE.
   The various procedures for abating nuisances prescribed by this chapter and
by other provisions of law and ordinance shall be cumulative one to the other,
and the city may elect to follow any such procedure which is applicable in
abating any particular nuisance.
(1999 Code, § 96.11)
SELECTED NUISANCES
§ 96.025 LITTERING.
   It is further declared to be unlawful for any person to litter any public or
private street, alley, driveway, parking lot or other property not his or her
own by throwing, dropping, laying or leaving bottles, cans, waste paper, trash
or other refuse in or upon such public or private property.
(1999 Code, § 96.28) Penalty, see §
96.999
ABANDONED VEHICLES
§ 96.040 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PERSON. Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
   PROPERTY. Any real property within the city which is not a street or
highway.
   STREET or HIGHWAY. The entire width between the boundary lines of every way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for
purposes of vehicular travel.
   VEHICLE. A machine propelled by power other than human power designed to
travel along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners or slides and
transport persons or property or pull machinery and shall include, without
limitation, automobile, truck, trailer, motorcycle, tractor, buggy and wagon.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011)
§ 96.041 ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES.
   No person shall abandon any vehicle within the city and no person shall
leave any vehicle at any place within the city for such time and under such
circumstances as to cause such vehicle reasonably to appear to have been
abandoned.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.042 LEAVING OF WRECKED, NONOPERATING VEHICLE IN STREET.
   No person shall leave any partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked or
junked vehicle or vehicle with an expired license tag on any street or highway
within the city.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.043 DISPOSITION OF WRECKED OR DISCARDED VEHICLES.
   (A)   No person in charge or control of any property within the city,
whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow any
partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked or junked, or discarded vehicle or
vehicle with an expired license tag to remain on such property.
   (B)   The owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise of any vehicle as
provided in this section shall first be given notice in writing or notice
posted on a vehicle to remove such dismantled, non operating, wrecked, junked
or discarded vehicle or unlicensed vehicle from their property. If such owner,
tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow such vehicle to remain on
said property longer than 72 hours after the expiration or written notice, the
Chief of Police or other officer shall cause the vehicle to be impounded as
provided.
   (C)   Except that this subchapter shall not apply with regard to a vehicle
in an enclosed building; a vehicle on the premises of a business or enterprise
operated in a lawful place and in a lawful manner, when necessary to the
operation of such business or enterprise; or a vehicle in an appropriate
storage place or depository maintained in a lawful place and manner by the
city.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.044 IMPOUNDING.
   The Chief of Police, or other appropriate official, or any member of the
Police Department designated by the Chief of Police, is hereby authorized to
remove or have removed any vehicle left at any place in the city which
reasonably appears to be in violation of this chapter or lost, stolen or
unclaimed; or whenever the driver or the person in charge of any vehicle is
placed under arrest and taken into custody and detained by police under
circumstances which leave or will leave a vehicle unattended on public
property, the vehicle shall be impounded until lawfully claimed or disposed of
in accordance with applicable ordinances. A Police Department record of the
impoundment and disposition of vehicles under this subchapter shall be
completed and retained and shall contain a description of the vehicle including
its condition, the circumstances of the impoundment, and an inventory of all
personal property contained in the vehicle.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011)
§ 96.045 ICE BOXES AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the owner or the occupant of a residential
building, structure or property to utilize the city rights-of-way for street or
alley purposes, or other city-owned property adjacent to said residential
building, structure or property for the purpose of storing any abandoned motor
vehicle, icebox, refrigerator or other building rubbish or similar items. It
shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any residential building,
structure or other property to utilize or use city premises including rights-
of-way for alleys and streets of such residential property for the use as a
place of repair for any automobiles or other household appliances. It shall be
the duty and responsibility of such owner or occupant of such residential
property to remove from the city premises, including rights-of-way, all such
abandoned items as listed above which were placed on the said property by the
owner or occupant.
   (B)   For the purpose of this section, an ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE is defined
as one that is in a state of disrepair and incapable of being moved under its
own power.
(Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
WEEDS AND TRASH
§ 96.060 TRASH AND WEEDS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful to allow the accumulation of trash or the growth of
weeds upon any property to include adjoining alleyways, street rights-of-way or
easements in the city.
(Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.061 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CLEANING. The removal of trash from property.
   OWNER. The owner of record as shown by the most current tax rolls of the
County Treasurer.
   TRASH. Any refuse, litter, ashes, leaves, debris, paper, combustibles,
rubbish, offal or waste of any kind or form which is uncared for, discarded or
abandoned.
   WEED.
      (1)   Includes, but is not limited to, poison ivy, poison oak or poison
sumac and all vegetation at any state of maturity which:
         (a)   Exceeds 12 inches in height, except healthy trees, shrubs or
products for human consumption grown in a tended and cultivated garden unless
such trees and shrubbery by their density or location, constitute a detriment
to the health, benefit and welfare of the public and community or a hazard to
traffic or create a fire hazard to the property or otherwise interfere with the
mowing of said weeds;
         (b)   Regardless of height, harbors, conceals or invites deposits or
accumulation of refuse or trash;
         (c)   Harbors rodents or vermin;
         (d)   Gives off unpleasant or noxious odors;
         (e)   Constitutes a fire or traffic hazard;
         (f)   Is dead or diseased;
         (g)   Is on any adjoining statutory, dedicated or accepted street
right-of-way;
         (h)   Is on any adjoining dedicated or accepted easement; or
         (i)   Is on any adjoining dedicated or accepted alleyway.
      (2)   The term WEED shall not include tended crops on land zoned for
agricultural use which are planted more than 150 feet from a parcel zoned for
other than agricultural use.
(Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-2011)
§ 96.062 EXEMPTION.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply to any property zoned and
used for agricultural purposes.
(Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-2011)
§ 96.063 ABATEMENT PROCEDURES.
   The City Mayor, or his or her designee, may cause property within the city
limits to be cleaned of trash and weeds and grass, to be cut or mowed, in
accordance with the following procedures.
   (A)   At least ten days’ notice shall be given to the owner of the property
by mail at the address shown by the current year’s tax rolls in the County
Treasurer’s office or posted on property, or handed to owner, occupant, owner’s
agent or the property manager, before the City Mayor, or his or her designee,
holds a hearing or takes action. The notice shall order the property owner to
clean the property of trash, or to cut or mow the weeds or grass on the
property, as appropriate, and said notice shall further state that unless such
work is performed within ten days of the date of the notice the work shall be
done by the city, and a notice of lien shall be filed with the County Clerk
against the property for the costs due and owing the city. At the time of the
mailing of the notice to the property owner, the city shall obtain a receipt of
mailing from the postal service, which receipt shall indicate the date of the
mailing and the name and address of the mailee. However, if the property owner
cannot be located within ten days from the date of mailing, notice may be given
by posting a copy of the notice on the property or by publication, as defined
in 11 O.S. § 1-102, one time not less than ten days prior to any hearing or
action by the City Mayor, or his or her designee. If the City Mayor, or his or
her designee, anticipates summary abatement of a nuisance in accordance with
the provisions of division (G) below, the notice, whether by mail or
publication, shall state, that any accumulation of trash or excessive weed or
grass growth on the owner’s property occurring within six months from and after
the date of this notice may be summarily abated by the municipal governing
body; that the costs of such abatement shall be assessed against the owner; and
that a lien may be imposed on the property to secure such payment, all without
further prior notice to the property owner.
   (B)   The owner of the property may give his or her written consent to the
City Mayor, or his or her designee, authorizing the removal of the trash or the
mowing of the weeds or grass and consenting to the payment of the actual cost
of such removal as provided by an estimate provided by the City Mayor or his or
her designee. By giving said written consent, the owner waives his or her right
to a hearing.
   (C)   A hearing may be held by the City Mayor, or his or her designee, to
determine whether the condition of this property meets the definition of §
96.061 and whether the condition of this property has become detrimental to the
health, benefit and welfare of the public and the community or a hazard to
traffic, or creates a fire hazard to the danger of the property.
   (D)   Upon a finding that the condition of the property constitutes a
detriment or hazard, and that the property will be benefitted by the removal of
such conditions, the City Mayor or his or her designee shall be granted the
right of entry on the property for the removal of trash, mowing of weeds or
grass, and performance of such necessary duties as the governmental function of
the city. Immediately following the cleaning or mowing of the property, the
City Clerk shall file a notice of lien with the County Clerk describing the
property and the work performed by the municipality, and stating that the city
claims a lien on said property for the cleaning and/or mowing costs.
   (E)   The City Mayor, or his or her designee, shall determine the actual
cost of such cleaning and mowing and any other expenses as may be necessary in
connection therewith, including the cost of notice and mailing. The City Clerk
shall forward, by mail, to the owner specified in division (A) above, a
statement of such actual cost and demanding payment. If the cleaning and mowing
are done by the City, the cost to the owner for said cleaning and mowing shall
not exceed the actual cost of the labor, maintenance and equipment required. If
the cleaning and mowing are done on a private contract basis, the work shall be
done by a vendor maintained on a certified list by the City Mayor, and such
vendor shall be selected on a rotating basis, Should the estimate for the work
exceed the sum of $2,000, the contract shall be awarded to the lowest and best
bidder under the provisions of the State Competitive Bidding Law, being 61 O.S.
§§ 101 et seq.
   (F)   (1)   If payment is not made within 30 days from the date of the
mailing of the statement, the City Clerk shall forward a certified statement of
the amount of the cost to the County Treasurer of the county in which the
property is located and the same shall be levied on the property and collected
by the County Treasurer as other taxes authorized by law. Until fully paid, the
cost and the interest thereon shall be the personal obligation of the property
owner from and after the date the cost is certified to the County Treasurer. In
addition, the cost and interest thereon shall be a lien against the property
from the date the cost is certified to the County Treasurer, co-equal with the
liens of ad valorem taxes and all other titles and liens against the property,
and the lien shall continue until the costs are paid in full.
      (2)   At any time prior to the collection as provided in this division
(F), the city may pursue any civil remedy for collection of the amount owing
and interest thereon, including an action in personam against the property
owner and an action in rem to foreclose its lien against the property. A
mineral interest, if severed from the surface interest, and not owned by the
surface owner, shall not be subject to any tax or judgment lien created
pursuant to this section. Upon receiving payment, if any, the City Clerk shall
forward to the County Treasurer a notice of such payment and directing
discharge of the lien.
   (G)   If the City Mayor, or his or her designee, causes property within the
city limits to be cleaned and weeds or grass to be mowed or cut in accordance
with the procedure provided for in divisions (A) through (F) above, any
subsequent accumulations of trash or excessive weed or grass growth on the
property occurring within a six-month period may be declared to be a nuisance
and may be summarily abated without further prior notice to the owner. At the
time of each summary abatement, the city shall notify the owner of the
abatement and the costs thereof. The notice shall state that the owner may
request a hearing within the next ten days after the date of mailing the
notice. The notice and hearing shall be as provided for in division (A) above.
Unless otherwise determined at the hearing, the cost of such abatement shall be
determined and collected as provided for in divisions (E) and (F) above;
provided however that this division (G) shall not apply if the records of the
County Clerk show the property was transferred after notice was given pursuant
to division (A) above.
   (H)   The owner of any property shall have the right to appeal to the City
Council any order of the City Mayor, or his or her designee, as specified in
divisions (A) through (G) above and such an appeal shall be taken by filing
written notice of appeal with the City Clerk within ten days after the order of
the City Mayor or his or her designee is rendered.
   (I)   If written notice of appeal is filed within ten days of the City Mayor
or his or her designee’s decision, the matter shall be heard by the City
Council for final decision.
(Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.064 ADMINISTRATIVE FEES.
   In addition to penalties provided in this chapter, an administrative fee of
$150 shall be charged and assessed against the owner. An additional fee of $75
shall be charged and assessed against the owner if the property has been
previously abated. The fee shall be in addition to all costs incurred for
abatement.
(Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-2011)
HEALTH NUISANCES
§ 96.075 HEALTH NUISANCES.
   (A)   Prohibited. No owner or occupant of any premises shall allow thereon
any source of filth, cause of sickness, condition conductive to the breeding of
insects or rodents that might contribute to the transmission of disease, or any
other condition adversely affecting the public health. Any such condition is
hereby declared a health nuisance and may be abated as provided in this
subchapter.
   (B)   Abatement order. Whenever the Director of the County Health Department
or any of its authorized representatives finds any of the health nuisances
specified in division (A) above upon any premises within city limits, he or she
shall have the owner or occupant of such premises, at his or her own expense,
to abate the health nuisance within 24 hours, or within such other time as
might be reasonable, and failure to do so shall constitute an offense. Such
order shall be in writing and may be served personally on the owner or occupant
of the premises, or authorized agent thereof, or a copy thereof may be left at
the last usual place of abode of such owner, occupant or agent, if known and
within the state, if the premises are unoccupied and the residence of such
owner, occupant or agent is unknown, or is without the state, such order may be
served by posting a copy thereof on the premises, or by publication in at least
one issue of a newspaper having general circulation within the county. If the
order of abatement is not complied with, the Mayor, or his or her designee, may
cause the order to be executed by the city and the city shall collect the costs
of such execution as provided by this section.
   (C)   Collection of costs. If it is necessary for the Director or his or her
authorized representative to execute the order of abatement as provided in this
subchapter, the Director of the County Health Department shall certify the cost
of abatement to the City Clerk, and to the owner, occupant or agent of the
property on which the condition existed. Such notice of cost shall be served in
accordance with the procedure provided for in the service of orders of
abatement, and shall grant the owner, occupant or agent 20 days in which to pay
the cost to the City Clerk. Then the City Clerk shall certify the costs to the
County Clerk who shall add them to the ad valorem taxes assessed against the
property. The costs shall then be a lien against the property until paid, and
shall be collected in the same manner as ad valorem taxes against the property.
Upon collection of the costs, they shall be paid to the city for reimbursements
of the funds used to pay such costs.
   (D)   Subchapter supplemental; emergency actions.
      (1)   The provisions of this subchapter shall be supplemental to all
ordinances.
      (2)   The provisions of this subchapter shall not prohibit the immediate
abatement or confiscation by an officer of the city or his or her authorized
representative, if conditions exist which threaten to imperil or endanger the
immediate health of the public.
(Ord. 2010-8, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.076 OFFICERS MAY ENTER PREMISES.
   (A)   Some public nuisances are of such nature as to constitute a grave and
immediate danger to the public peace, health, safety, morals or welfare. It is
recognized that circumstances may be as such to justify, and even require, the
City Mayor or other appropriate officer or agency of the city government to
take immediate and proper action to abate such nuisances, or to reduce or
suspend said danger until more deliberate action can be taken toward such
abatement.
   (B)   The City Mayor, the officers and employees of the Health Department,
the Police Department and the Fire Department, and city officers and employees
concerned with inspection of buildings, plumbing and electrical or other
installations, may enter any structure or premises at any reasonable time to
determine whether any hazard to life, property or public welfare or any public
nuisance exists.
(Ord. 2010-8, passed 1-10-2011)
§ 96.077 ABATEMENT OF PUBLIC NUISANCES.
   (A)   The Chief of the Fire Department, the Chief of Police, the City
Attorney, the City Health Officer, the Building Inspector, the Electrical
Inspector, the Plumbing Inspector or any other officer subordinate to the City
Mayor, may submit, through or with the consent of the City Mayor, to the City
Council, a statement as to the existence of a public nuisance as defined in §
96.001 or any other section of this code, and a request or recommendation that
it may be abated. The City Mayor himself or herself, any Council member or any
resident or residents of the city may submit such a statement and request or
recommendation to the City Council. The Council shall determine whether or not
the alleged public nuisance is a public nuisance in fact. For the purpose of
gathering evidence on the subject, the Council shall have the power to subpoena
and examine witnesses, books, papers and other effects. Before proceeding to
abate the nuisance or to have it abated, the Council shall give notice of a
hearing on the proposed abatement to the owner of any property concerned and to
any persons alleged or deemed responsible for or to be causing the public
nuisance, and an adequate opportunity to be heard if such notice and
opportunity for a hearing can be given. Such notice to the owner and other
persons concerned shall be given in writing by mail or by service by a police
officer if their names and addresses are known; but, if their names and
addresses are not known, and the public peace, health, safety, morals and
welfare would not be unduly jeopardized by the necessary delay, a notice of the
hearing shall be published in a newspaper of general circulation within the
city.
   (B)   If the Council finds that a public nuisance does in fact exist, it
shall direct the owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing the
public nuisance to abate it within a specified time if the public interest
would not be unduly jeopardized by the consequent delay; or if the owner or
other persons responsible for or causing the public nuisance do not abate it
within the specified time, the Council shall direct the City Mayor to abate the
public nuisance or to have it abated if summary abatement is practical. The
City Clerk shall send a statement of the cost of such summary abatement to the
owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing the nuisance, as may be
just under the circumstances, if their names and addresses are known. Until
paid, such cost shall constitute a debt to the city collectible as other debts
may be collected.
   (C)   If the owner or other persons responsible for a public nuisance does
not abate it as directed, and if summary abatement is deemed impractical, the
Council by resolution shall direct the bringing of a suit to the District Court
to abate the public nuisance.
   (D)   The procedures for abating or dealing with public nuisances as
prescribed in this section, shall be cumulative and in addition to any other
procedures authorized by law or ordinance.
(Ord. 2010-8, passed 1-10-2011) Penalty, see §
96.999
§ 96.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter by doing any act
prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or declared to be a nuisance, an
offense or misdemeanor thereby, or who fails to do any act required by any such
provision, or who fails to do any act when such provision declares such failure
to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor, or who violates any legal
order or regulation made pursuant to this chapter, or who maintains any
nuisance as defined in this chapter, is guilty of an offense, and upon
conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in §
10.99. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed a separate
offense.
   (B)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
96.040 through
96.045 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction there of
shall be punished as set forth in division (A) above. Each day such violation
is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and
shall be punishable as such hereunder.
   (C)   In addition to the abatement procedure set forth in §
96.063, any person, firm or corporation violating the provisions of §§
96.060 through
96.064 shall be guilty of an offense and upon conviction for such violation
shall be punished as set forth in division (A) above.
   (D)   Every person, firm or corporation who shall violate any provision of
§§
96.075 through
96.077 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof shall be
punished as set forth in §
10.99. Each day a violation continues, after due notice has been served in
accordance with the terms and provisions hereof, shall be deemed a separate
offense.
(1999 Code, § 96.99) (Ord. 2010-8, passed 1-10-2011; Ord. 2010-9, passed 1-10-
2011; Ord. 2010-11, passed 1-10-2011)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 97.01 BENCH MARK ESTABLISHED.
   The block placed at the immediate corner of the First National Bank Building
and marked “Bench Mark, City of Hooker”, level 100, shall be and the same is
hereby established as a permanent bench mark for said city.
(1999 Code, § 97.01)
§ 97.02 DATUM PLANE.
   All ordinances referring to streets, curbing, paving, grading and
elevations, water mains and laterals, and sewer mains and laterals where
elevations or vertical distances are given shall have reference to said datum
plane, and elevations or vertical distances given in feet shall signify so many
feet above said datum plane, unless otherwise expressed.
(1999 Code, § 97.02)
USE AND OBSTRUCTION OF STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
§ 97.15 TREES AND SHRUBBERY.
   (A)   Trees and shrubbery to be trimmed.
      (1)   The owner of any premises abutting on any street of this city shall
trim all trees and shrubbery growing in the parking, between the sidewalks and
the roadway, of any such street, and all trees and shrubbery growing on any
part of the premises adjacent to the sidewalks or any street or alley, in such
manner that the boughs or limbs thereof shall not obstruct free and convenient
passage and travel along the streets, sidewalks and alleys. When such premises
are occupied by some person other than the owner, such occupant shall trim the
trees and shrubbery in the same manner as hereinbefore required of the owner.
Such trees and shrubbery shall be trimmed so that the lowest branches or
foliage shall not be lower than ten feet above the roadway of a street or
alley, nor lower than eight feet above the sidewalk.
      (2)   Any owner or occupant who fails, refuses or neglects to trim trees
and shrubbery as provided in division (A) above, after receiving five days’
notice from the Mayor or Street Superintendent to do so, shall be guilty of an
offense against the city. Every day that the owner or occupant fails, refuses
or neglects to trim such trees or shrubbery, after the expiration of five days’
notice, shall be a separate offense.
   (B)   Unlawful to injure trees and shrubbery. It is unlawful for any person
to injure any tree or shrubbery on a street or alley in the city, provided that
this shall not prohibit the lawful and proper care and removal of such trees
and shrubbery.
(1999 Code, § 97.15) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.16 BUSINESS USE OF STREETS AND THE LIKE.
   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to construct, erect,
place, operate, maintain or permit to exist any icebox, ice dock, gasoline
pump, gasoline storage reservoir, tire rack, tire tools or equipment, water
hose connection or mercantile business, or any tools, stand, equipment,
merchandise or appurtenances thereof, aerials, poles or wires therefor, whether
permanent or temporary, or any other obstruction, upon any part of any street,
alley, boulevard, parkway, curbing or parking within the city.
(1999 Code, § 97.16) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.17 OBSTRUCTION OF STREETS AND SIDEWALKS.
   It is unlawful for any person to use or obstruct the sidewalks of the city
in any manner so as to interfere unduly with pedestrian traffic thereon, or to
use or obstruct the streets and alleys of the city in any manner so as to
interfere unduly with lawful traffic and parking thereon.
(1999 Code, § 97.17) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.18 TRASH.
   It is unlawful for any person to deposit, throw or sweep into or upon a
street, alley, parking or sidewalk of the city any paper, rubbish, grass,
weeds, tree trimmings, dirt, trash, crates, boxes or other refuse of any kind.
(1999 Code, § 97.18) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.19 PLAYING ON STREETS AND SIDEWALKS.
   It is unlawful for any person to play on the sidewalks or upon the main-
traveled portion of the streets and alleys of the city, except as may be
authorized by ordinance.
(1999 Code, § 97.19) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.20 WATER AND OTHER FLUIDS.
   (A)   Water, mud and the like from vehicle not to drain onto street. No
automobile or other vehicle shall be washed at any place within the city where
the water, dirt, mud or other substances removed therefrom by or during the
washing thereof will drain into or upon any street or sidewalk of the city.
   (B)   Water and the like from filling stations and other businesses. It is
unlawful for any owner or operator of a filling station or other place of
business, or any agent or employee thereof, to cause or allow water, grease or
other fluid to flow or drain into, upon, over or across any sidewalk, parking,
street, alley or other public way.
   (C)   Water from air conditioners and the like. It is unlawful for any
person, firm or corporation to permit water from any air conditioner, cooler or
hydrant to drain upon any sidewalk, street, gutter, alley or pavement within
the city.
(1999 Code, § 97.20) Penalty, see §
10.99
Cross-reference:
   Nuisances enumerated, see §
96.003
§ 97.21 SIDEWALK HAZARDS; LIABILITY.
   It is unlawful for the owner or occupant of property abutting upon a
sidewalk or sidewalk area to permit the sidewalk or sidewalk area adjacent to
the property to become a hazard to persons using the sidewalk or sidewalk area.
(1999 Code, § 97.21) Penalty, see §
10.99
EXCAVATIONS
§ 97.35 PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE.
   (A)   Prior to any building, construction, digging or excavating, an
application shall be made to the City Clerk who will then have the city’s code
enforcement officer review the application and determine if the proposed action
falls in compliance with city codes. Such application shall give all necessary
details in connection with proposed construction, digging or excavation; a full
description of the exact location where such work is contemplated, and such
other information as may be required. Such application and permit shall be made
on forms prescribed by the City Clerk and a fee of $34.50 shall be charged for
the permit. The permit shall be in effect for one year commencing from the date
of approval.
   (B)   Prior to digging, ditching or any kind of excavation on any property,
the occupant and/or owner of the property inside the city limits, for the
purpose of utilities, building, and construction must also call OKIE ONE CALL
(811) (“Call Before You Dig”) to report proposed action; a description of the
exact location where such work is contemplated and such other information as
may be required. “ONE CALL” will contact all utility and phone servers
including other companies with underground lines who will locate lines to the
property for safety. The lines will be located up to the owner’s property line.
(1999 Code, § 97.35) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.36 BOND.
   In addition to the permit required in §
97.35, a bond, cash or surety to the city in an amount of not less than $300
conditioned on the replacement of the pavement, curbing, guttering and sidewalk
in as good a condition as they were prior to the ditching through of such
street, sidewalk or alley may be required. The bond shall be in force and
effect for a period of two years from the date of the permit. At the end of
that time, on proper application, the bond may be withdrawn, provided that the
City Clerk certifies to the fact that the replaced paving, curbing and/or
sidewalk appears to be in as good a condition as it would have been had it not
been ditched through or otherwise disturbed. Otherwise, the city shall use the
bond money so deposited for the repair of the street, alley or sidewalk so
ditched through or otherwise disturbed; provided, however, that if, in the
judgment of the City Clerk, a $300 bond will be insufficient to repair the
damage likely to occur, then he or she may require a bond in an amount which in
his or her opinion will be sufficient to repair the damaged street, and
provided, further, however, that any party aggrieved by the decision of the
City Clerk shall have the right to appeal such decision to the Mayor and
Council and in all cases its decision shall be final.
(1999 Code, § 97.36)
§ 97.37 BARRICADES.
   In addition to the bond required, any party seeking a permit as herein
provided must also agree to erect suitable and plainly marked barriers
sufficient to advise and restrain the public from the use of the portion of the
sidewalk, alley or street being ditched through or otherwise disturbed.
(1999 Code, § 97.37)
§ 97.38 LIABILITY IN EXCESS OF BOND AMOUNT.
   Nothing in this subchapter shall be construed to relieve any person from
liability he or she has incurred by reason of damage to the streets, alleys and
sidewalks in a greater amount than the bond which such party has posted.
(1999 Code, § 97.38)

LICENSING
§ 110.01 APPLICABILITY TO EX-SERVICE PERSONS.
   Nothing in this chapter or in other ordinances of the city shall be deemed
to require ex-service persons to secure a license or pay a license fee for
engaging in a business, occupation or privilege when he or she is exempted
therefrom by 72 O.S. §§ 1 through 6 or other provisions of state law.
(1999 Code, § 110.01) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008)
§ 110.02 LICENSE TAX FOR CERTAIN BUSINESSES.
   A business license procured through the City Clerk’s office is hereby levied
on every business engaging in exercising or pursuing any business, profession,
trade, occupation or privileges in this city, in the amounts respectively
indicated.
   (A)   The City Clerk’s office must have on file a copy of the business’s
sales tax permit. After a business owner or operator applies for a business
license and follows the requirement, a license will then be issued to the
business from the city.
   (B)   A license tax is hereby levied on every person engaging in, exercising
or pursuing any of the following businesses, professions, trades, occupations
or privileges in this city, in the amounts respectively indicated: for each
itinerant peddler, solicitor or photographer, $10 per day, $20 per week, $50
per month, or $75 annually; provided that this shall not apply to persons
selling farm or garden produce produced by themselves in the county or any
county adjacent thereto.
   (C)   A license tax is hereby levied on outdoor advertisement (billboards)
in the city: for initial permit application, $50; for permit renewal
(biennial), $20; (new) outdoor advertising license, $200; for outdoor
advertising license renewal, $100; and for late license filing with renewal due
date of June 30 of each year, $25 penalty.
(1999 Code, § 110.02) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008; Ord. 2011-4, passed 9-6-
2011)
§ 110.03 LICENSES.
   (A)   Licenses required. It is unlawful for any person to engage in,
exercise or pursue any business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege for
which a license tax is levied by §
110.02 or by any other ordinance or ordinance provision without paying the
license tax, and securing and possessing a valid license therefore.
   (B) Issuance of license. Upon making proper application to the City Clerk,
the payment of the license tax and fulfillment of any other condition which may
be prescribed by law or ordinance, the City Clerk shall issue a license
therefore. Such license taxes shall be credited to the General Fund of the
city.
   (C)   Term of license; tax amount. Annual licenses shall expire December 31
of the year for which they are issued. When an annual license is issued after
August 31 of the year to a person just beginning to engage in, exercise or
pursue a business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege, the January 1
deadline will be waived for one time, with that person renewing the business
license on or before December 31 one year from the date they have received a
business license.
   (D)   Separate licenses required. Every person who engages in, exercises or
pursues a business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege for which a
license is required, at or from more than one place in the city, or who engages
in, exercises or pursues more than one such business, profession, trade,
occupation or privilege, shall pay the fee and secure a separate license, for
each such place or for each such business, profession, trade, occupation or
privilege.
(1999 Code, § 110.03) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008; Ord. 2011-4, passed 9-6-
2011) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.04 LICENSE DISPLAY.
   Every holder of a license to engage in, exercise or pursue a business,
profession, trade, occupation or privilege shall conspicuously display the
license at all times in some part of his or her place of business or activity,
shall carry the license and shall display it to any person who requests to see
it, provided that, in lieu of the above manner of displaying such licenses,
when licenses are required for coin-operated music or amusement devices,
vending machines and similar devices and equipment, the license may be placed
on or attached to such device or equipment in such position and manner that it
will be clearly visible and shall be so placed or attached if the license so
states on its face. It is unlawful to fail or refuse to display the license as
required in this section.
(1999 Code, § 110.04) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.05 LICENSE REVOCATION.
   Any license issued by the city to any person to engage in, exercise or
pursue any business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege may be revoked
by the Council after adequate opportunity for a hearing, for the following
reasons:
   (A)   The licensee is engaging in, exercising or pursuing the business,
profession, trade, occupation or privilege in such a manner that he or she has
created or is creating a public nuisance as defined by 50 O.S. §§ 1 and 2; or
   (B)   Serious or repeated violation of the law or ordinances.
(1999 Code, § 110.05) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008)
§ 110.06 LICENSE TRANSFERABILITY.
   The assignment or transfer of licenses is prohibited in 11 O.S. § 22-107,
and hence assignment or transfer or licenses shall not be permitted in this
city.
(1999 Code, § 110.06) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008)
§ 110.07 LICENSE REPLACEMENT; FEE.
   (A)   Whenever any license to engage in, exercise or pursue a business,
profession, trade, occupation or privilege has been lost or destroyed without
any wrongful act or connivance by the holder, the City Clerk, on application,
shall issue a duplicate license for the unexpired time.
   (B)   The fee for every duplicate license issued, payable to the City Clerk,
shall be $10.
(1999 Code, § 110.07) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008)
GENERAL REGULATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS
§ 110.20 WEIGHTS AND MEASURES.
   It is unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale any food, fuel,
clothing or any other commodity which does not weigh or measure fully as much,
according to standard weights or measures of the state, as the weight or
measure for which it is sold or offered for sale.
(1999 Code, § 110.20) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008) Penalty, see §
10.99
Cross-reference:
   Unwholesome food; misbranded food, see 94.05
§ 110.21 LOUDSPEAKERS AND THE LIKE; PERMITS.
   (A)   Permit required. It is unlawful for any person or persons, firm or
corporation to operate any public address system, loud speaker or mechanical
voice amplifier on the streets of the city or on the outside of any building in
the city.
   (B)   Application for permit. Any person, persons, firm or corporation
desiring to use or operate a public address system, a loud speaker or any
mechanical voice amplifier upon the streets of the city or on the outside of
any building in the city between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. shall
first make a written application to the City Council by filing the same with
the City Clerk, stating the hours during which the applicant desires to operate
the public address system, loud speaker or mechanical voice amplifier, and the
location thereof, The application shall be acted upon by the City Council at
its next regular meeting or at an adjourned meeting or a special meeting called
for that purpose.
(1999 Code, § 110.21) (Ord. 2008-04, passed 12-1-2008) Penalty, see §
10.99

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   All of the terms and phrases used in this chapter shall be given the
same use and meaning as defined by the State Alcoholic Beverage Control Act,
37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et seq.
   (B)   All references in this chapter to the State Alcoholic Beverage Control
Board shall be deemed to mean the ABLE Commission.
(1999 Code, § 111.01) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72, passed 1-6-1986)
§ 111.02 OCCUPATION TAX.
   (A)   Occupation tax levied.
      (1)   There is hereby levied an annual occupation tax upon each person,
firm or corporation engaged within this city in any of the following
occupations hereinafter named, in the following sums respectively set opposite
the designation of each occupation:
Occupation Tax
Occupation         Tax
Brewer             $1,000
Class B wholesaler $500
Distiller          $2,500
Oklahoma winemaker $50
Package store      $100
Rectifier          $2,500
Wholesaler         $2,000
Winemaker          $500
 
      (2)   The above occupation taxes for brewer and Class B wholesaler shall
be reduced by 75% if the licensee is also holder of a state license to
manufacture or wholesale, as the case may be, any nonintoxicating malt
beverages as provided in the state statutes.
   (B)   Payment required.
      (1)   Any state licensee originally entering upon any occupation herein
listed shall pay the tax therefor at the office of the City Clerk on or before
the date upon which he or she enters upon such occupation. Said licensee shall
provide a copy of his or her current state license before payment of an
occupation tax will be accepted. Thereafter, the licensee shall pay the tax
annually on or before April 1.
      (2)   The occupation tax subject to this section shall be prorated on a
monthly basis for the year in which an occupation begins operations.
      (3)   Upon payment of the said occupation tax, the City Clerk shall issue
a receipt to said state licensee, which said licensee shall post in a
conspicuous place on the premises wherein he or she carries on his or her
occupation.
      (4)   Any person who engages in any of the occupations taxed by this
section without paying said occupation tax imposed therefor in advance of such
operation is guilty of an offense against the city and upon conviction thereof
shall be penalized as provided in §
111.99.
   (C)   Expiration date; proration.
      (1)   All occupation tax levies under the provisions of this section
expire on March 31 of each year.
      (2)   The amount of any occupation tax levied shall be computed pro rata
upon the months remaining in the year ending March 31 following. Such taxes
paid on or before the fifteenth day of any month shall be on the basis of the
first day of the month, and such taxes paid after the fifteenth day of any
month shall be on the basis of the first day of the next succeeding month.
   (D)   Not to operate until tax has been paid. No brewer, distiller,
winemaker, Oklahoma winemaker, rectifier, wholesaler, Class B wholesaler or
retail package store shall do business, or offer to do business, in this city
until the occupation tax levied by this section has been paid in full to the
City Clerk and receipt issued therefor.
(1999 Code, § 111.02) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72, passed 1-6-1986; Ord.
92, passed 12-7-1992) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.03 ANNUAL REPORT OF CITY CLERK.
   The City Clerk shall make an annual report to the ABLE Commission covering
the fiscal year and showing the number and class of licensees subject to the
occupation tax and the amount of money collected from said tax.
(1999 Code, § 111.03) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72, passed 1-6-1986)
§ 111.04 CERTIFICATES OF COMPLIANCE; FEE.
   (A)   Application for certificate; investigations.
      (1)   Every applicant for a certificate of compliance with the zoning,
fire, health and safety codes of this city required by 37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et
seq. shall apply at the office of the City Clerk by:
         (a)   Filing a written application on forms prescribed by that office;
and
         (b)   Paying a verification and certification fee in the amount of $20
at the time of filing.
      (2)   Upon receipt of an application for a certificate of compliance the
City Clerk shall cause an investigation to be made to determine whether the
premises proposed for licensed operations comply with the provisions of the
zoning ordinance and any health, fire, building and other safety codes
applicable to it.
      (3)   The city shall act on all such applications within 20 days of
receipt thereof.
   (B)   Issuance of certificates.
      (1)   Upon finding that the premises of an applicant for a certificate
are in compliance with all applicable zoning ordinances, a certificate of
zoning shall be issued to the ABLE Commission.
      (2)   Upon finding that the premises of an applicant for a certificate
are in compliance with all applicable fire, safety and health codes, a
certificate of compliance shall be issued to the ABLE Commission.
      (3)   The above certificates of compliance shall be signed by the Mayor
or by the City Clerk.
(1999 Code, § 111.04) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72, passed 1-6-1986)
§ 111.05 HOURS OF SALE AND OPERATION.
   (A)   No package store licensee shall sell or keep a package store premises
open for the purpose of selling any alcoholic beverages at any hour other than
between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 9:00 p.m. Monday through Saturday.
   (B)   No alcoholic beverages may be sold, dispensed, served or consumed on
the premises of a mixed drink beverage licensee between the hours of 2:00 a.m.
and 10:00 a.m. No licensee shall permit any person who has in his or her
possession an open container, having as its contents a non-intoxicating or
intoxicating alcoholic beverage, to remain in a mixed beverage establishment
between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 10:00 a.m. No person having in his or her
possession an open container, having as its contents low-point beer or an
intoxicating alcoholic beverage, shall remain in a mixed beverage establishment
between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 10:00 a.m. For the purpose of this section,
the term OPEN CONTAINER shall mean any receptacle containing a non-intoxicating
or intoxicating alcoholic beverage and includes the original container of the
beverage where the original seal has been broken or opened.
   (C)   The provisions of division (B) of this section shall not apply to the
licensee of such mixed beverage establishment, musicians loading or unloading
instruments or performing or rehearsing for performances to be held on such
premises, construction workers and maintenance and repair personnel performing
their individual trades upon the premises, or delivery persons making
deliveries to the premises.
(37 O.S. § 591) (1999 Code, § 111.05) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72,
passed 1-6-1986) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.06 AGE-RELATED OFFENSES.
   (A)   It is an offense for any person under the age of 21 years to be
employed in the selling or handling of alcoholic beverages within this city.
   (B)   It is an offense to sell, furnish or give any alcoholic beverage to
any person under 21 years of age, or to any intoxicated, insane or mentally
deficient person.
   (C)   It is an offense to permit any person under 21 years of age to enter
into, remain within or loiter about the premises of any retail package store.
   (D)   It is an offense for any person to misrepresent his or her age in
writing or by presenting false documentation of age for the purpose of inducing
any person to sell him or her an alcoholic beverage.
(1999 Code, § 111.06) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.07 ADVERTISING.
   It is an offense for any person to advertise, or cause to be advertised, in
any manner, the sale of alcoholic beverages, except as specifically permitted
by the provisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, 37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et
seq.
(1999 Code, § 111.07) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.08 SALES AND CONSUMPTION.
   (A)   Separate premises required. It is an offense for any person to
maintain, operate or assist in any manner in the maintenance or operation of a
retail package store unless the premises are separated from adjoining premises
on which any other goods, wares or merchandise is sold or services are
rendered, by nontransparent walls, broken only, if at all, by a passageway to
which the public is not admitted.
   (B)   Beverage not to be taken through passageway for sale. It is an offense
for any person to take any alcoholic beverage through any passageway described
in division (A) above for the purpose of selling or reselling such beverage, or
for the purpose of delivery thereof in connection with a sale of such
beverages.
   (C)   How beverage is to be sold; not to consume on premises.
      (1)   It is an offense for any person to sell or deliver any alcoholic
beverages at a retail alcoholic beverage store other than:
         (a)   In retail containers;
         (b)   At ordinary room temperatures;
         (c)   In the original package; and
         (d)   For consumption off the premises.
      (2)   It is an offense for any person to permit any alcoholic beverage to
be consumed, or any retail container of such beverage to be broken or opened,
on the premises of any retail package store.
   (D)   Person not to consume on premises. It is an offense for any person to
drink or consume in any manner any alcoholic beverage on the premises of a
retail alcoholic beverage store or to open or break the seal of any original
package or retail container containing alcoholic beverages on such premises.
   (E)   To be sold only in retail stores and the like. It is an offense for
any person to sell at retail, or to deliver in consequence or in completion of
any such a sale, any alcoholic beverages at or to any place in the city except
at a retail alcoholic beverage store, in strict conformity with this subchapter
and the laws of this state.
   (F)   Not to sell on credit. It is an offense for any person to sell at
retail, or to sell at any retail alcoholic beverage store, any alcoholic
beverage on credit.
   (G)   Not to give prizes and the like. It is an offense for any person to
offer or to furnish any prize, premium, gift or similar inducement to any
customer or consumer in connection with the sale or attempted sale of any
alcoholic beverage.
(1999 Code, § 111.08) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.09 LOCATION OF ALCOHOL-RELATED BUSINESSES.
   It is an offense for any person to own, operate, maintain or be interested
in any manner in any establishment mentioned in §
111.02(A)(1) at a place within the city which is forbidden as a location for
such establishment by the laws of this state or by the ordinances of this city.
(1999 Code, § 111.09) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.10 TRANSPORTATION OF ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES.
   It is an offense for any person to transport in any vehicle upon any public
highway, street or alley any alcoholic beverage, unless such alcoholic beverage
is:
   (A)   In an unopened original container with seal unbroken and the original
cap or cork not removed from the container; or
   (B)   In the trunk or other closed compartment or other container, out of
public view and out of reach of the driver or any occupant of the vehicle.
(1999 Code, § 111.10) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.11 HOURS OF WHOLESALE SALE AND DELIVERY.
   It is an offense for any person to sell or deliver to any retail alcoholic
beverage store any amount of spirits, wines or other kind or alcoholic beverage
on Saturday of any week, on Sunday of any week, on New Year’s Day, on Memorial
Day, on the Fourth of July, on Labor Day, on Thanksgiving Day, on Christmas Day
or while the polls are open on the day of any general, primary, primary run-off
or special election, whether national, state, county or city.
(1999 Code, § 111.11) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.12 INTOXICATED PERSONS NOT TO BE PERMITTED IN RESTAURANTS AND THE LIKE.
   It is an offense for any person, whether as owner, manager, operator or
employee of any café, restaurant, club or any place of recreation within the
city, to permit any person to be or to become drunk or intoxicated or to be
under the influence of intoxicating drink at such place.
(1999 Code, § 111.12) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.13 REGULATING THE SALE OF LOW-POINT BEER AND ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES FOR IN-
SITE CONSUMPTION.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to offer for sale, or otherwise
distribute, for consumption on the premises any low-point beer and/or alcoholic
beverages. Violations of this section shall be punishable by fine or
imprisonment, or both, as allowed by applicable law. Each act of violation
shall be considered a separate offense.
   (B)   Subject to applicable state law, a person may offer for sale low-point
beer and/or alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises if and only if:
      (1)   The person operates a business in the same premises whereby 80% of
the gross revenue from that business is derived from the sale of food for meals
eaten on the premises; and
      (2)   The person has been duly licensed or permitted to sell both food
for consumption on the premises, as well as low-point beer and/or alcoholic
beverages for consumption on the premises according to all local, county and
state laws and regulations.
   (C)   The term “low-point beer” shall have the same definition as is defined
in 37A O.S. § 1-103v1. The terms “alcoholic beverage”, “person”, “premises” and
“meals” shall have the same definitions as they are defined in 37A O.S. § 1-
103v1.
(Ord. 145, passed 12-4-2006) Penalty, see §
111.99
NONINTOXICATING BEVERAGES
§ 111.25 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   NONINTOXICATING BEVERAGES. All beverages containing more than 0.5% of
alcohol by volume, and not more than 3.2% of alcohol by weight.
   RETAIL DEALER. All persons, firms, corporations, associations or
concessionaires who sell, distribute or dispense any nonintoxicating beverages
within the city, without regard as to any place where such beverage may be
consumed or used.
(1999 Code, § 111.25)
§ 111.26 HOURS OF SALE.
   It shall be unlawful and an offense for any retail dealer to sell or offer
for sale any nonintoxicating beverages for consumption on the premises between
the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m., excepting Saturday nights when such
beverages may not be sold between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. on the
following Monday.
(1999 Code, § 111.26) (Ord. 70, passed 8-5-1985) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.27 PROHIBITED SALES AND CONDUCT.
   It is unlawful for any retail dealer knowingly to sell, give away, trade,
exchange, supply or furnish nonintoxicating beverages to any person under age
21, or in any manner to do any act prohibited by the statutes of the state, or
to fail to do any act which is affirmatively required by the statutes of the
state respecting nonintoxicating beverages.
(1999 Code, § 111.27) (Ord. 63, passed 10-3-1983) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whenever in this chapter an act is prohibited or is made or declared
to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, or whenever in this chapter the
doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be
unlawful, where no specific penalty is provided therefor, the violation of any
provision of this chapter, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who engages in any of the occupations taxed by §
111.02 without paying said occupation tax imposed therefor in advance of such
operation is guilty of an offense against the city and upon conviction thereof
shall be fined the sum of not more than $500, excluding costs. Each day of such
violation shall constitute a separate offense.
(1999 Code, § 111.99) (Ord. 69, passed 8-5-1985; Ord. 72, passed 1-6-1986)
CHAPTER 112: HAZARDOUS BUSINESSES
Section
   
112.01   Oil and gas wells
   
112.02   Self-service stations
 
   
112.99   Penalty
§ 112.01 OIL AND GAS WELLS.
   (A)   Purpose. In the exercise of the police power of the city, this section
is enacted for the protection of persons and property against danger from fire
and explosion, and to protect the health of persons residing in the corporate
limits of the city from noisome, dangerous and noxious odors and vapors
incident to the drilling of oil and gas wells and the hazards arising from the
construction, erection, location and maintenance of well derricks, slush pits,
pipes or storage tanks and other similar structures and equipment incident or
appurtenant to the drilling, operation and maintenance of oil and gas wells.
   (B)   Not to be drilled within city and the like. No oil or gas well shall
be drilled, nor shall any oil or gas derrick, wellhead, slush pit, storage tank
or pipe or pipes connecting therewith, or similar structures appurtenant to any
oil or gas well, be erected, constructed or located within the corporate limits
of the city.
(1999 Code, § 113.01) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.02 SELF-SERVICE STATIONS.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      LIQUID. Any flammable and combustible liquid used as motor fuel or
otherwise.
      SELF-SERVICE STATION. The portion of property where liquids are stored
and subsequently dispensed from fixed approved dispensing equipment by persons
other than a service station attendant, and may include facilities available
for sale of other retail products.
   (B)   Employment of attendant. A self-service station shall have at least
one attendant on duty while the self-service station is open to the public. The
attendant shall be mentally and physically capable of performing the functions
and assuming the responsibilities prescribed to him or her in this section.
   (C)   Duties of attendant. Any attendant at a self-service station shall
supervise, observe and control the dispensing of liquids while such liquids are
actually being dispensed. He or she shall prevent the dispensing of liquids
into a portable container unless the container is of metal or is approved by
the office of the State Fire Marshal, has a tight closure with screwed or
spring cover, and is fitted or so designed that the contents can be poured
without spilling. The attendant shall control sources of ignition and
immediately handle accidental spills and fire extinguishers if needed.
   (D)   Dispensing area; clear view. The dispensing area shall at all times be
in clear view of the attendant and the placing or allowing of any obstacle to
come between the dispensing area and the attendant control area shall be
prohibited. The attendant shall at all times have voice communication with any
person in the dispensing area.
   (E)   Spillage; area design. Provision shall be made in the area where
liquids are dispensed to prevent spilled liquid from flowing into the interior
of self-service station buildings. Such provision may be made by grading
driveways, raising door sills or other equally effective means.
   (F)   Posting; operating instructions and warning signs. Operating
instructions and warning signs shall be conspicuously posted in the dispensing
area. Warning signs shall read:
IT IS UNLAWFUL AND DANGEROUS TO DISPENSE GASOLINE INTO UNAPPROVED CONTAINERS.
NO SMOKING. TURN OFF ENGINE.
   (G)   Emergency controls. In a self-service station, emergency controls
shall be installed at a location acceptable to the department having
jurisdiction, and shall not be more than 100 feet from the dispensers. The
emergency controls shall be clearly identified and easily accessible control
switches or circuit breakers remote from the dispensing services, including any
remote pumping system, that will shut off power to all dispensing devices in
the event of an emergency.
   (H)   Hose nozzle valves. Hose nozzle valves used at a self-service station
shall be an approved automatic-closing type without a latch-open device.
   (I)   Waste liquids; storage. Crankcase drainings and flammable or
combustible liquids shall not be dumped into sewers, streams or adjoining
property, but shall be stored in tanks or drums outside any building until
removed from the premises.
   (J)   Supplemental. The provisions of this section are intended to be
supplemental to any provisions of ordinances of the city relating to the public
health and safety and are intended to impose more stringent standards on the
construction and operation of self-service stations.
(1999 Code, § 113.02) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whenever in this chapter an act is prohibited or is made or declared
to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, or whenever in the chapter the
doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be
unlawful, where no specific penalty is provided therefor, the violation of any
provision of this chapter, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in §
10.99.
   (B)   (1)   Any person, firm, company or corporation violating any of the
terms and provisions of §
112.01 shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided in §
10.99. Each day during which any oil or gas well is drilled, or any derrick,
wellhead, slush pit, storage tank or pipe or pipes connecting therewith, are
operated or maintained in contravention of any provision of §
112.01 shall constitute a separate offense, and each oil or gas well drilled,
operated or maintained in violation of any provision of §
112.01, together with its incidental or appurtenant structures, shall likewise
be deemed a separate offense for each day.
      (2)   No fine or penalty prescribed by division (A) above shall be
exclusive of the rights of any person, firm, corporation or company residing in
or owning property within the corporate limits of this city to enforce any
provision of §
112.01 against any person, firm, corporation or company violating the
provisions thereof, by any legal means, including remedy of injunction.
(1999 Code, § 113.99)
CHAPTER 113: MEDICAL MARIJUANA
Section
   
113.01   Certificate of compliance
   
113.02   License
   
113.03   Exemption
 
   
113.99   Penalty
§ 113.01 CERTIFICATE OF COMPLIANCE.
   The City Clerk shall issue a certificate of compliance to an applicant for a
medical marijuana business license from the state, upon submission of an
application for certificate of compliance and evidence of compliance,
qualifying the proposed medical marijuana business at the proposed location.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-7-2020)
§ 113.02 LICENSE.
   (A)   There is hereby created the city medical marijuana business license,
which shall include the following categories:
      (1)   Medical marijuana commercial grower;
      (2)   Medical marijuana processor;
      (3)   Medical marijuana dispensary;
      (4)   Medical marijuana transporter; and
      (5)   Medical marijuana testing laboratory.
   (B)   A city medical marijuana business license may be issued to an
applicant upon presentation by the applicant of a medical marijuana business
license issued by the state and payment of the city medical marijuana business
license fee of $750.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-7-2020)
§ 113.03 EXEMPTION.
   Use or possession of medical marijuana or paraphernalia in compliance with
state law is exempt from the prohibition against use or possession of marijuana
and paraphernalia as provided in §
131.08.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-7-2020)
§ 113.99 PENALTY.
   Possession of up to four and one half ounces of marijuana by persons who can
state a medical condition, but not in possession of a state-issued medical
marijuana license, shall constitute a misdemeanor offense with a fine not to
exceed $400.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-7-2020)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 130.01 ADOPTION OF STATE LAW.
   (A)   Adoption of Oklahoma Criminal Laws. For the purpose of the safety of
the citizens, the City Council hereby adopts 21 O.S. §§ 1 et seq., Oklahoma
Criminal Laws.
   (B)   Authority of Police Department. The City Council hereby gives
authority to the Police Department, Police Chief and patrol officers to enforce
this code, conduct search and seizures, make arrests and issues citations for
violations.
   (C)   Authority of Municipal Judge. The city also directs the Municipal
Judge to enforce the code, as the law allows for a municipality.
   (D)   Authority of City Attorney. The city also directs the Municipal
Attorney to prosecute violators of the code.
(21 O.S. § 42) (1999 Code, § 130.01) (Ord. 91, passed 5-4-1992)
GENERAL OFFENSES
§ 130.15 ATTEMPT TO COMMIT OFFENSE.
   Every person who attempts to commit an offense against the ordinances of the
city and in such attempt does any act toward the commission of such offense,
but fails or is prevented or intercepted in the perpetration thereof, is guilty
of an offense, and shall be punished not exceeding one-half the longest term of
imprisonment and not exceeding one-half the largest fine prescribed for the
attempted offense itself.
(1999 Code, § 130.15)
§ 130.16 AIDING AND ABETTING.
   When no punishment for counseling, aiding or abetting in the commission of a
particular offense is expressly prescribed by ordinance, every person who
counsels, aids or abets another in the commission of such is guilty of an
offense and punishable in the same manner as the principal offender.
(1999 Code, § 130.16)
